   <h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">
    List of people who disappeared mysteriously
   </h1>
   <div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
    <div id="siteSub">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div>
    <div id="contentSub">
     <span class="mw-redirectedfrom">
      (Redirected from
      <a href="/w/index.php?title=Unexplained_disappearances&amp;redirect=no" title="Unexplained disappearances">
       Unexplained disappearances
      </a>
      )
     </span>
    </div>

          <img alt="" data-file-height="204" data-file-width="262" height="39" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/50px-Question_book-new.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/75px-Question_book-new.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/9/99/Question_book-new.svg/100px-Question_book-new.svg.png 2x" width="50"/>

        <span class="mbox-text-span">
         This article
         <b>

           verification
          </a>
         </b>
         .
         <span class="hide-when-compact">
          Please help
          <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit">
           improve this article
          </a>
          by
          <a href="/wiki/Help:Introduction_to_referencing/1" title="Help:Introduction to referencing/1">

           (June 2015)

        </span>
       </td>
      </tr>

     <div class="hatnote">
      This article is about individual persons who have disappeared.  For disappearances associated with ships, see
      <a href="/wiki/List_of_missing_ships" title="List of missing ships">
       List of missing ships
      </a>
      .  For disappearances associated with aircraft, see
      <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_aerial_disappearances" title="List of aerial disappearances">
       List of aerial disappearances
      </a>
      .
     </div>
     <p>
      This is a
      <b>
       list of people who disappeared mysteriously
      </b>
      , and whose current whereabouts are unknown or whose deaths are not substantiated, as well as a few cases of people whose disappearance was notable and remained mysterious for a long time, but was eventually explained.
     </p>
     <p>
     </p>

         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-61">
          <a href="#2011">
           <span class="tocnumber">
            13.12
           </span>
           <span class="toctext">
            2011
           </span>
          </a>
         </li>
         <li class="toclevel-2 tocsection-62">
          <a href="#2012">
           <span class="tocnumber">
            13.13
           </span>
           <span class="toctext">
            2012
           </span>
          </a>
         </li>
        </ul>
       </li>
       <li class="toclevel-1 tocsection-63">
        <a href="#Solved_cases">

         </span>

       </li>

     <p>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="Before_1800">
       Before 1800
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Before 1800">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       71 BC  Although he was presumed killed in battle during the
       <a href="/wiki/Third_Servile_War" title="Third Servile War">
        Third Servile War
       </a>
       , the body of the rebel slave
       <a href="/wiki/Spartacus" title="Spartacus">
        Spartacus
       </a>
       was never found and his fate remains unknown.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-1">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         1
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       53 BC 
       <a href="/wiki/Ambiorix" title="Ambiorix">
        Ambiorix
       </a>
       was, together with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Catuvolcus" title="Catuvolcus">
        Catuvolcus
       </a>
       , prince of the
       <a href="/wiki/Eburones" title="Eburones">
        Eburones
       </a>
       , leader of a
       <a href="/wiki/Belgae" title="Belgae">
        Belgic tribe
       </a>
       of northeastern
       <a href="/wiki/Gaul" title="Gaul">
        Gaul
       </a>
       (
       <a href="/wiki/Gallia_Belgica" title="Gallia Belgica">
        Gallia Belgica
       </a>
       ), where modern Belgium is located. According to the writer
       <a href="/wiki/Florus" title="Florus">
        Florus
       </a>
       (iii.10.8), Ambiorix and his men managed to cross the Rhine and disappeared without a trace.
      </li>
      <li>
       30 BC 
       <a href="/wiki/Caesarion" title="Caesarion">
        Caesarion
       </a>
       (Ptolemy XV Philopator Philometor Caesar) was the son of
       <a href="/wiki/Cleopatra" title="Cleopatra">
        Cleopatra
       </a>
       by
       <a href="/wiki/Julius_Caesar" title="Julius Caesar">
        Caesar
       </a>
       , and as such the last king of the Ptolemaic dynasty of Egypt, ruling alone for eleven days. His death at 17 on the orders of
       <a href="/wiki/Augustus" title="Augustus">
        Augustus
       </a>
       (while still Octavian) is accepted, and yet the exact circumstances of his death and the location of his body are not documented.
       <a href="/wiki/Plutarch" title="Plutarch">
        Plutarch
       </a>
       says that he was sent to India for safety by his mother and later lured back by the promise that Octavian would allow him nominal rule of Egypt. The fates of his younger half-brothers,
       <a href="/wiki/Alexander_Helios" title="Alexander Helios">
        Alexander Helios
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Ptolemy_Philadelphus_(son_of_Cleopatra)" title="Ptolemy Philadelphus (son of Cleopatra)">
        Ptolemy Philadelphus
       </a>
       , sons of Cleopatra by
       <a href="/wiki/Mark_Antony" title="Mark Antony">
        Mark Antony
       </a>
       , are also unknown.
      </li>
      <li>
       c. 67 
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle" title="Paul the Apostle">
        The Apostle Paul
       </a>
       , early Christian missionary whose
       <a href="/wiki/Pauline_epistles" title="Pauline epistles">
        letters to various congregations around the Mediterranean
       </a>
       make up much of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_Testament" title="New Testament">
        New Testament
       </a>
       . He spent 6062 under
       <a href="/wiki/House_arrest" title="House arrest">
        house arrest
       </a>
       after
       <a href="/wiki/Paul_the_Apostle#His_final_days_spent_in_Rome" title="Paul the Apostle">
        arriving in Rome
       </a>
       to appeal his earlier conviction in
       <a href="/wiki/Caesarea_Maritima" title="Caesarea Maritima">
        Caesarea
       </a>
       to Caesar; after that it is assumed that he helped
       <a href="/wiki/Saint_Peter" title="Saint Peter">
        St. Peter
       </a>
       set up the Roman church, but neither the Bible nor any other sources say anything about his life afterwards.
       <a href="/wiki/Ignatius_of_Antioch" title="Ignatius of Antioch">
        St. Ignatius
       </a>
       , writing over 50 years later, suggested he had been martyred by the Romans.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-2">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         2
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Christian tradition holds that he was beheaded under Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Nero" title="Nero">
        Nero
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-3">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         3
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       108164 
       <a href="/wiki/Legio_IX_Hispana" title="Legio IX Hispana">
        Legio IX Hispana
       </a>
       (Ninth Spanish Legion) was a legion said to have disappeared in Britain during the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_conquest_of_Britain" title="Roman conquest of Britain">
        Roman conquest of Britain
       </a>
       , although archaeology has shown the legion was subsequently transferred to mainland Europe.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bowman_4-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Bowman-4">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         4
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many references to the legion have been made in subsequent works of fiction.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-5">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         5
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       378  Roman Emperor
       <a href="/wiki/Valens" title="Valens">
        Valens
       </a>
       was
       <a href="/wiki/Gothic_War_(376%E2%80%93382)" title="Gothic War (376382)">
        defeated by the Goths
       </a>
       at the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Adrianople" title="Battle of Adrianople">
        Battle of Adrianople
       </a>
       (modern Edirne, Turkey). The body of Valens was never found.
      </li>
      <li>
       <abbr title="circa">
        c.
       </abbr>
       <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
        834
       </span>
       
       <a href="/wiki/Muhammad_ibn_Qasim_(al-Alawi)" title="Muhammad ibn Qasim (al-Alawi)">
        Muhammad ibn Qasim (al-Alawi)
       </a>
       led a rebellion against the Abbasid Caliphate but was defeated and detained. He was able to flee but was never heard from again.
      </li>
      <li>
       1021 
       <a href="/wiki/Al-Hakim_bi-Amr_Allah" title="Al-Hakim bi-Amr Allah">
        Al-Hakim bi-Amr Allah
       </a>
       (36), sixth
       <a href="/wiki/Fatimid_Caliphate" title="Fatimid Caliphate">
        Fatimid
       </a>
       caliph and 16th
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ismailism" title="Ismailism">
        Ismaili
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Imam" title="Imam">
        imam
       </a>
       , rode his donkey to the Muqattam hills outside Cairo for one of his regular nocturnal meditation outings and failed to return. A search found only the donkey and his bloodstained garments.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-6">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         6
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1071 
       <a href="/wiki/Hereward_the_Wake" title="Hereward the Wake">
        Hereward the Wake
       </a>
       was a formerly exiled Anglo-Danish minor noble rebel who led a huge revolt in the marshy region of
       <a href="/wiki/Ely,_Cambridgeshire" title="Ely, Cambridgeshire">
        Ely
       </a>
       in England against the rule of
       <a href="/wiki/William_the_Conqueror" title="William the Conqueror">
        William the Conqueror
       </a>
       . Eventually betrayed by fearful local monks who led the Norman troops through secret trackways, many rebels were mutilated or executed, but Hereward escaped, never to be heard of again.
      </li>
      <li>
       1203 
       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_I,_Duke_of_Brittany" title="Arthur I, Duke of Brittany">
        Arthur, Duke of Brittany
       </a>
       , an heir to the throne of England. He was supported by French nobility who did not want
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/John_of_England" title="John of England">
        John of England
       </a>
       as overlord. On 31 July 1202, while besieging his grandmother
       <a href="/wiki/Eleanor_of_Aquitaine" title="Eleanor of Aquitaine">
        Eleanor of Aquitaine
       </a>
       , Arthur was surprised and captured by John's barons and imprisoned at
       <a href="/wiki/Falaise,_Calvados" title="Falaise, Calvados">
        Falaise
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Normandy" title="Normandy">
        Normandy
       </a>
       . The following year, Arthur was transferred to
       <a href="/wiki/Rouen" title="Rouen">
        Rouen
       </a>
       and then vanished mysteriously in April 1203.
      </li>
      <li>
       <abbr title="circa">
        c.
       </abbr>
       <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
        1291
       </span>
       
       <a href="/wiki/Vandino_and_Ugolino_Vivaldi" title="Vandino and Ugolino Vivaldi">
        Vandino and Ugolino Vivaldi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Republic_of_Genoa" title="Republic of Genoa">
        Genoese
       </a>
       sailors and explorers lost while attempting the first oceanic journey from Europe to Asia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-7">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         7
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1412 
       <a href="/wiki/Owain_Glynd%C5%B5r" title="Owain Glyndr">
        Owain Glyndr
       </a>
       , the last native
       <a href="/wiki/Welsh_people" title="Welsh people">
        Welsh person
       </a>
       to hold the title
       <a href="/wiki/Prince_of_Wales" title="Prince of Wales">
        Prince of Wales
       </a>
       , instigated the Welsh Revolt against the rule of
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_IV_of_England" title="Henry IV of England">
        Henry IV of England
       </a>
       in 1400. Although initially successful, the uprising was eventually put down, but Glyndr disappeared and was never captured, betrayed, or tempted by royal pardons.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-8">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         8
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1483  The
       <a href="/wiki/Princes_in_the_Tower" title="Princes in the Tower">
        Princes in the Tower
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_V_of_England" title="Edward V of England">
        Edward V of England
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_of_Shrewsbury,_1st_Duke_of_York" title="Richard of Shrewsbury, 1st Duke of York">
        Richard of Shrewsbury, first duke of York
       </a>
       (9), sons of King
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_IV_of_England" title="Edward IV of England">
        Edward IV of England
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Elizabeth_Woodville" title="Elizabeth Woodville">
        Elizabeth Woodville
       </a>
       , were placed in the
       <a href="/wiki/Tower_of_London" title="Tower of London">
        Tower of London
       </a>
       (which at that time served as a fortress and a royal palace as well as a prison) by their uncle
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_III_of_England" title="Richard III of England">
        Richard III of England
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-9">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         9
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The remains of four children have been found which could be the princes, but neither has been subjected to DNA analysis to positively identify them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guardian2013_10-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Guardian2013-10">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         10
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Neither was ever seen in public again and their fate remains unknown.
      </li>
      <li>
       1499 
       <a href="/wiki/John_Cabot" title="John Cabot">
        John Cabot
       </a>
       , Italian explorer, disappeared along with his five ships during an expedition to find a
       <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage" title="Northwest Passage">
        western route
       </a>
       from Europe to Asia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-11">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         11
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1501 
       <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Corte-Real" title="Gaspar Corte-Real">
        Gaspar Corte-Real
       </a>
       , Portuguese explorer, disappeared on an expedition to discover the
       <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage" title="Northwest Passage">
        Northwest Passage
       </a>
       from Europe to Asia. Two of his ships returned to Lisbon, but the third, with Gaspar on board, was lost and never heard from again.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-12">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         12
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1502 
       <a href="/wiki/Miguel_Corte-Real" title="Miguel Corte-Real">
        Miguel Corte-Real
       </a>
       , Portuguese explorer, disappeared while searching for his brother
       <a href="/wiki/Gaspar_Corte-Real" title="Gaspar Corte-Real">
        Gaspar
       </a>
       . Like his brother, he took three ships, and as with his brother, the ship with Miguel on board was lost and never heard from again.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-13">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         13
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1526 
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Hoces" title="Francisco de Hoces">
        Francisco de Hoces
       </a>
       , Spanish sailor, was commander of the
       <i>
        San Lesmes
       </i>
       , one of the seven ships of the Loasa Expedition under
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Garc%C3%ADa_Jofre_de_Loa%C3%ADsa" title="Garca Jofre de Loasa">
        Garca Jofre de Loasa
       </a>
       . It has been speculated that
       <i>
        San Lesmes
       </i>
       , last seen in the Pacific in late May, may have reached
       <a href="/wiki/Easter_Island" title="Easter Island">
        Easter Island
       </a>
       or any of the
       <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">
        Polynesian archipelagos
       </a>
       , or even
       <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">
        New Zealand
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">
        <a href="#cite_note-14">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         14
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">
        <a href="#cite_note-15">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         15
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1546 
       <a href="/wiki/Francisco_de_Orellana" title="Francisco de Orellana">
        Francisco de Orellana
       </a>
       , Spanish explorer and conquistador, disappeared while exploring the Amazon in November. His fate remains a mystery.
      </li>
      <li>
       1578 
       <a href="/wiki/Sebastian_of_Portugal" title="Sebastian of Portugal">
        Sebastian of Portugal
       </a>
       , Portuguese King, whose body was never found after the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Alc%C3%A1cer_Quibir" title="Battle of Alccer Quibir">
        Battle of Alccer Quibir
       </a>
       ; many Portuguese came to believe that Sebastian had survived the battle and would return to claim his throne. The
       <a href="/wiki/Sebastianism" title="Sebastianism">
        belief
       </a>
       arose that Sebastian could return at any moment to help Portugal in its darkest hour.
      </li>
      <li>
       <abbr title="circa">
        c.
       </abbr>
       <span style="white-space:nowrap;">
        1590
       </span>
        The
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_colonists_at_Roanoke" title="List of colonists at Roanoke">
        Roanoke colonists
       </a>
       disappeared, becoming known as the
       <a href="/wiki/Roanoke_Colony" title="Roanoke Colony">
        Lost Colony
       </a>
       . On 18 August 1590, their settlement was found abandoned.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">
        <a href="#cite_note-16">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         16
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1611 
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Hudson" title="Henry Hudson">
        Henry Hudson
       </a>
       was an English explorer and seafarer. He discovered New York Harbor for the
       <a href="/wiki/Dutch_East_India_Company" title="Dutch East India Company">
        Dutch East India Company
       </a>
       . In 1611, mutineers set him, his son, and six others adrift in a small boat in what is now
       <a href="/wiki/Hudson_Bay" title="Hudson Bay">
        Hudson Bay
       </a>
       . They were never seen again.
      </li>
      <li>
       1628 
       <a href="/wiki/History_of_New_Hampshire#Founding:_1600.E2.80.931775" title="History of New Hampshire">
        David Thompson
       </a>
       , founder of New Hampshire in 1623. He moved his family to an island in
       <a href="/wiki/Boston_Harbor" title="Boston Harbor">
        Boston Harbor
       </a>
       (today called
       <a href="/wiki/Thompson_Island_(Massachusetts)" title="Thompson Island (Massachusetts)">
        Thompson Island
       </a>
       in his honor) in 1626, becoming the first European settlers of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Boston,_Massachusetts" title="Boston, Massachusetts">
        Boston, Massachusetts
       </a>
       . He disappeared in 1628 and was never heard from again. Some historians theorize he was the victim of foul play. Others suggest he accidentally drowned in Boston Harbor.
      </li>
      <li>
       1696 
       <a href="/wiki/Henry_Every" title="Henry Every">
        Henry Every
       </a>
       was an English pirate who vanished after perpetrating one of the most profitable pirate raids in history; despite a worldwide manhunt and an enormous bounty on his head, Every was never heard from again.
      </li>
      <li>
       1788 
       <a href="/wiki/Aim%C3%A9e_du_Buc_de_Riv%C3%A9ry" title="Aime du Buc de Rivry">
        Aime du Buc de Rivry
       </a>
       , daughter of a wealthy plantation owner on the French island of
       <a href="/wiki/Martinique" title="Martinique">
        Martinique
       </a>
       . After being sent to a convent school in France, she was returning home in July or August 1788 when the ship she was on vanished at sea. It is thought that the ship was attacked and taken by
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Barbary_corsairs" title="Barbary corsairs">
        Barbary pirates
       </a>
       . It has been suggested that she was enslaved and eventually sent to
       <a href="/wiki/Istanbul" title="Istanbul">
        Istanbul
       </a>
       as a gift to the
       <a href="/wiki/Ottoman_Empire" title="Ottoman Empire">
        Ottoman
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Sultan" title="Sultan">
        sultan
       </a>
       by the
       <a href="/wiki/Bey" title="Bey">
        Bey
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Algiers" title="Algiers">
        Algiers
       </a>
       . It is unconfirmed if she was the same person as
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Naksh-i-Dil_Haseki" title="Naksh-i-Dil Haseki">
        Naksh-i-Dil Haseki
       </a>
       , consort of the sultan.
      </li>
      <li>
       1788  The French expedition of
       <a href="/wiki/Jean-Fran%C3%A7ois_de_Galaup,_comte_de_Lap%C3%A9rouse" title="Jean-Franois de Galaup, comte de Laprouse">
        Jean-Franois de Galaup, comte de Laprouse
       </a>
       disappeared after a last stop off Botany Bay (near what is now Sydney, Australia). The wrecks of the expedition's two ships were subsequently discovered near
       <a href="/wiki/Vanikoro" title="Vanikoro">
        Vanikoro
       </a>
       , where the survivors may have set up a camp.
      </li>
      <li>
       1792 
       <a href="/wiki/James_Harrod" title="James Harrod">
        James Harrod
       </a>
       , 46, an early explorer of the areas west of the
       <a href="/wiki/Appalachian_Mountains" title="Appalachian Mountains">
        Appalachian Mountains
       </a>
       prior to their settlement by European-Americans, never returned from a trip to western
       <a href="/wiki/Kentucky" title="Kentucky">
        Kentucky
       </a>
       from
       <a href="/wiki/Harrodsburg,_Kentucky" title="Harrodsburg, Kentucky">
        Harrodsburg
       </a>
       . Theories about his fate range from murder at the hands of his companions or native Americans in the area, to accidental death or a desire to abandon his wife and family.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1800_to_1899">
       1800 to 1899
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: 1800 to 1899">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       1803 
       <a href="/wiki/George_Bass" title="George Bass">
        George Bass
       </a>
       (32), was a British explorer of
       <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">
        Australia
       </a>
       , who set sail from Sydney for South America and was never heard from again.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">
        <a href="#cite_note-17">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         17
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1809 
       <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Bathurst_(diplomat)" title="Benjamin Bathurst (diplomat)">
        Benjamin Bathurst
       </a>
       (25), a British diplomat, disappeared from an inn in
       <a href="/wiki/Perleberg" title="Perleberg">
        Perleberg
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1812 
       <a href="/wiki/Theodosia_Burr_Alston" title="Theodosia Burr Alston">
        Theodosia Burr Alston
       </a>
       (29), daughter of U.S. Vice President
       <a href="/wiki/Aaron_Burr" title="Aaron Burr">
        Aaron Burr
       </a>
       and sometimes called the most educated American woman of her day, sailed from
       <a href="/wiki/Georgetown,_South_Carolina" title="Georgetown, South Carolina">
        Georgetown, South Carolina
       </a>
       , aboard the
       <i>
        Patriot
       </i>
       , which was never seen again.
      </li>
      <li>
       1826 
       <a href="/wiki/William_Morgan_(anti-Mason)" title="William Morgan (anti-Mason)">
        William Morgan
       </a>
       (52), resident of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Batavia_(city),_New_York" title="Batavia (city), New York">
        Batavia, New York
       </a>
       , disappeared just before his book critical of
       <a href="/wiki/Freemasonry" title="Freemasonry">
        Freemasonry
       </a>
       was published.
      </li>
      <li>
       1829 
       <a href="/wiki/John_Lansing,_Jr." title="John Lansing, Jr.">
        John Lansing, Jr.
       </a>
       (75), an American politician, left his
       <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">
        Manhattan
       </a>
       hotel to mail a letter at a
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
        New York City
       </a>
       dock and was never seen again.
      </li>
      <li>
       1843 
       <a href="/wiki/Sequoyah" title="Sequoyah">
        Sequoyah
       </a>
       (
       <i>
        circa
       </i>
       73), the creator of
       <a href="/wiki/Cherokee_syllabary" title="Cherokee syllabary">
        Cherokee syllabary
       </a>
       , disappeared during a trip to Mexico to locate isolated tribes of Cherokees who had moved there during the time of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_Removal" title="Indian Removal">
        Indian Removal
       </a>
       in the U.S. His body has never been found, although at least three different burial sites have been reported.
      </li>
      <li>
       1845 
       <a href="/wiki/Franklin%27s_lost_expedition" title="Franklin's lost expedition">
        Franklin's lost expedition
       </a>
       , with more than 100 seamen, made last contact with a whaling ship before entering
       <a href="/wiki/Victoria_Strait" title="Victoria Strait">
        Victoria Strait
       </a>
       in search of the
       <a href="/wiki/Northwest_Passage" title="Northwest Passage">
        Northwest Passage
       </a>
       . Although the remains of some individuals were later discovered, the majority of corpses were never found, and the exact reason for their demise remains a mystery.
      </li>
      <li>
       1848 
       <a href="/wiki/Khachatur_Abovian" title="Khachatur Abovian">
        Khachatur Abovian
       </a>
       (38), an Armenian writer and national public figure of the early 19th century, credited as creator of modern
       <a href="/wiki/Armenian_literature" title="Armenian literature">
        Armenian literature
       </a>
       , left his house early one morning and was never heard from again.
      </li>
      <li>
       1848 
       <a href="/wiki/Ludwig_Leichhardt" title="Ludwig Leichhardt">
        Ludwig Leichhardt
       </a>
       (34), Prussian explorer and naturalist, disappeared during his third major expedition to explore parts of northern and central Australia. He was last seen on 3 April at McPherson's Station on the
       <a href="/wiki/Darling_Downs" title="Darling Downs">
        Darling Downs
       </a>
       , en route from the
       <a href="/wiki/Condamine_River" title="Condamine River">
        Condamine River
       </a>
       to the
       <a href="/wiki/Swan_River_(Western_Australia)" title="Swan River (Western Australia)">
        Swan River
       </a>
       . His fate after moving inland, although investigated by many, remains a mystery.
      </li>
      <li>
       1849 
       <a href="/wiki/S%C3%A1ndor_Pet%C5%91fi" title="Sndor Petfi">
        Sndor Petfi
       </a>
       (26),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hungarian_people" title="Hungarian people">
        Hungarian
       </a>
       poet and
       <a href="/wiki/Classical_liberalism" title="Classical liberalism">
        liberal
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Revolutionary" title="Revolutionary">
        revolutionary
       </a>
       , was one of the key figures of the
       <a href="/wiki/Hungarian_Revolution_of_1848" title="Hungarian Revolution of 1848">
        Hungarian Revolution of 1848
       </a>
       . Petfi was last seen in
       <a href="/wiki/Transylvania" title="Transylvania">
        Transylvania
       </a>
       during the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Segesv%C3%A1r" title="Battle of Segesvr">
        Battle of Segesvr
       </a>
       . Although different theories and rumours abound about his supposed death or deportation to
       <a href="/wiki/Siberia" title="Siberia">
        Siberia
       </a>
       , neither his body nor genuine records to support the theories were ever found.
      </li>
      <li>
       1857 
       <a href="/wiki/Solomon_Northup" title="Solomon Northup">
        Solomon Northup
       </a>
       (4849?), American author, is most notable for his book
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Twelve_Years_a_Slave" title="Twelve Years a Slave">
         Twelve Years a Slave
        </a>
       </i>
       , in which he details his kidnapping and subsequent sale into slavery. Northup did not return to his family from his book-promoting tour. No contemporary evidence documents Northup after 1857. Historians are divided on whether Northup was kidnapped once again and sold back into slavery or simply died of natural causes.
      </li>
      <li>
       1857 -
       <a href="/wiki/Nana_Sahib" title="Nana Sahib">
        Nana Sahib
       </a>
       (33), an Indian aristocrat. As a leader of the
       <a href="/wiki/Indian_Rebellion_of_1857" title="Indian Rebellion of 1857">
        Indian Rebellion of 1857
       </a>
       he disappeared after the
       <a href="/wiki/East_India_Company" title="East India Company">
        East India Company
       </a>
       's forces retook his city of
       <a href="/wiki/Kanpur" title="Kanpur">
        Kanpur
       </a>
       . Rumours that he had died of an illness or fled to exile in
       <a href="/wiki/Nepal" title="Nepal">
        Nepal
       </a>
       or another part of
       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
        India
       </a>
       were never proven.
      </li>
      <li>
       1865  Captain
       <a href="/wiki/James_William_Boyd" title="James William Boyd">
        James William Boyd
       </a>
       (43), a
       <a href="/wiki/Confederate_States_of_America" title="Confederate States of America">
        Confederate States of America
       </a>
       military officer, vanished after his release as a
       <a href="/wiki/Prisoner_of_war" title="Prisoner of war">
        prisoner of war
       </a>
       in February 1865, as he failed to show up for a rendezvous with his son to go to Mexico at the end of the
       <a href="/wiki/American_Civil_War" title="American Civil War">
        American Civil War
       </a>
       . Boyds disappearance was at the center of a
       <a href="/wiki/Conspiracy_theory" title="Conspiracy theory">
        conspiracy theory
       </a>
       that he was killed in the place of
       <a href="/wiki/John_Wilkes_Booth" title="John Wilkes Booth">
        John Wilkes Booth
       </a>
       , the assassin of President Abraham Lincoln.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guttridge_18-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Guttridge-18">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         18
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1872  Captain
       <a href="/wiki/Benjamin_Briggs" title="Benjamin Briggs">
        Benjamin Briggs
       </a>
       (37), his wife Sarah Elizabeth (31), their daughter Sophia Matilda (2), and all seven crew members were missing when the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Mary_Celeste" title="Mary Celeste">
         Mary Celeste
        </a>
       </i>
       was found adrift in choppy seas some 400 miles (640km) east of the
       <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">
        Azores
       </a>
       . Their unexplained disappearances are at the core of "one of the most durable mysteries in nautical history".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">
        <a href="#cite_note-19">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         19
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1874 
       <a href="/wiki/Charley_Ross" title="Charley Ross">
        Charley Ross
       </a>
       , age 4, a resident of Philadelphia, was enticed along with his brother Walter into a horse-drawn carriage while playing in their front yard on 1 July. Walter got out at a fireworks shop, and the carriage drove on without him. The family received ransom notes and worked with police, to no avail.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">
        <a href="#cite_note-20">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         20
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">
        <a href="#cite_note-21">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         21
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1880s 
       <a href="/wiki/William_Cantelo" title="William Cantelo">
        William Cantelo
       </a>
       , inventor of an early machine gun, never returned to his
       <a href="/wiki/Southampton" title="Southampton">
        Southampton
       </a>
       home after one of his frequent and lengthy sales trips. His sons speculated years later that he may have re-emerged as
       <a href="/wiki/Hiram_Maxim" title="Hiram Maxim">
        Hiram Maxim
       </a>
       , another machine-gun pioneer, whom he strongly resembled.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-William_Cantelo_22-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-William_Cantelo-22">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         22
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1880 
       <a href="/wiki/Lamont_Young" title="Lamont Young">
        Lamont Young
       </a>
       , a government geologist inspecting new gold fields on behalf of the New South Wales Mines Department, together with his assistant, Max Schneider, boat owner Thomas Towers, and two other men, all disappeared near
       <a href="/wiki/Bermagui,_New_South_Wales" title="Bermagui, New South Wales">
        Bermagui, New South Wales
       </a>
       , Australia.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23">
        <a href="#cite_note-23">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         23
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The location where the abandoned wreck of their boat was discovered was subsequently named
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mystery_Bay" title="Mystery Bay">
        Mystery Bay
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">
        <a href="#cite_note-24">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         24
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1888 
       <a href="/wiki/Boston_Corbett" title="Boston Corbett">
        Boston Corbett
       </a>
       (56), the
       <a href="/wiki/Union_Army" title="Union Army">
        Union Army
       </a>
       soldier who fatally shot
       <a href="/wiki/John_Wilkes_Booth" title="John Wilkes Booth">
        John Wilkes Booth
       </a>
       , later went insane and was incarcerated in a mental asylum in 1887. He escaped from the facility a year later and was never seen again, though some historians suspect he may have perished in the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Hinckley_Fire" title="Great Hinckley Fire">
        Great Hinckley Fire
       </a>
       of 1 September 1894.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herald_25-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Herald-25">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         25
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kubicek_26-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Kubicek-26">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         26
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1890 
       <a href="/wiki/Louis_Le_Prince" title="Louis Le Prince">
        Louis Le Prince
       </a>
       (48),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Motion_picture" title="Motion picture">
        motion picture
       </a>
       pioneer, disappeared after boarding a Paris-bound train at
       <a href="/wiki/Dijon" title="Dijon">
        Dijon
       </a>
       , France.
      </li>
      <li>
       1892 
       <a href="/wiki/Hermann_Fol" title="Hermann Fol">
        Hermann Fol
       </a>
       , 46, Swiss
       <a href="/wiki/Zoology" title="Zoology">
        zoologist
       </a>
       regarded as the father of modern
       <a href="/wiki/Cell_biology" title="Cell biology">
        cell biology
       </a>
       , disappeared with several crewmembers of his yacht shortly after leaving
       <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9nodet" title="Bnodet">
        Bnodet
       </a>
       , France.
      </li>
      <li>
       1896 
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Jennings_Fountain" title="Albert Jennings Fountain">
        Albert Jennings Fountain
       </a>
       (57), a former
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Texas_State_Senate" title="Texas State Senate">
        Texas state senator
       </a>
       and lieutenant governor of that state, disappeared near
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Cruces,_New_Mexico" title="Las Cruces, New Mexico">
        Las Cruces, New Mexico
       </a>
       , United States, along with his son Henry (8) on February 1. Evidence found along their route strongly suggests they were murdered, but no bodies were ever found.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1900s">
       1900s
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: 1900s">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       1900  Three
       <a href="/wiki/Lighthouse" title="Lighthouse">
        lighthouse
       </a>
       keepers working on the
       <a href="/wiki/Flannan_Isles" title="Flannan Isles">
        Flannan Isles
       </a>
       (off the northwestern coast of Scotland) disappeared in a mystery commemorated in the ballad
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Flannan_Isle" title="Flannan Isle">
         Flannan Isle
        </a>
       </i>
       and the opera
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Lighthouse_(opera)" title="The Lighthouse (opera)">
         The Lighthouse
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1902 
       <a href="/wiki/Yda_Hillis_Addis" title="Yda Hillis Addis">
        Yda Hillis Addis
       </a>
       , (45), a translator of ancient Mexican narratives, was never seen after escaping from an insane asylum in California that her husband had gotten her confined to during their divorce.
      </li>
      <li>
       1909 
       <a href="/wiki/Joshua_Slocum" title="Joshua Slocum">
        Joshua Slocum
       </a>
       (65), Canadian-American
       <a href="/wiki/Sailor" title="Sailor">
        sailor
       </a>
       and first man to
       <a href="/wiki/Single-handed_sailing" title="Single-handed sailing">
        sail single-handedly
       </a>
       around the world (18951898), disappeared after setting sail from Vineyard Haven on
       <a href="/wiki/Martha%27s_Vineyard" title="Martha's Vineyard">
        Martha's Vineyard
       </a>
       alone, bound for
       <a href="/wiki/South_America" title="South America">
        South America
       </a>
       , aboard the same 36ft 9in (11.20m)
       <a href="/wiki/Sloop" title="Sloop">
        sloop
       </a>
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Spray_(sailing_vessel)" title="Spray (sailing vessel)">
         Spray
        </a>
       </i>
       he had used for his circumnavigation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27">
        <a href="#cite_note-27">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         27
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1910s">
       1910s
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: 1910s">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       1910 
       <a href="/wiki/Dorothy_Arnold" title="Dorothy Arnold">
        Dorothy Arnold
       </a>
       (25),
       <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">
        Manhattan
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Socialite" title="Socialite">
        socialite
       </a>
       and perfume heiress, vanished after buying a book in New York City. She intended to walk through Central Park, but was never seen again.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28">
        <a href="#cite_note-28">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         28
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1912 
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bobby_Dunbar" title="Bobby Dunbar">
        Bobby Dunbar
       </a>
       (4) disappeared during a fishing trip in
       <a href="/wiki/St._Landry_Parish,_Louisiana" title="St. Landry Parish, Louisiana">
        St. Landry Parish, Louisiana
       </a>
       . A child found in the custody of William Cantwell Walters of
       <a href="/wiki/Mississippi" title="Mississippi">
        Mississippi
       </a>
       some eight months later was ruled to be Bobby Dunbar by a court-appointed arbiter, and Walters was found guilty of
       <a href="/wiki/Kidnapping" title="Kidnapping">
        kidnapping
       </a>
       . The child grew up as Bobby Dunbar, had four children of his own, and died in 1966. In 2004,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Genetic_fingerprinting" title="Genetic fingerprinting">
        DNA tests
       </a>
       proved that the child found was not related to Bobby Dunbar's brother, Alonzo.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29">
        <a href="#cite_note-29">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         29
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1914 
       <a href="/wiki/Ambrose_Bierce" title="Ambrose Bierce">
        Ambrose Bierce
       </a>
       (71), American writer known for "
       <a href="/wiki/An_Occurrence_at_Owl_Creek_Bridge" title="An Occurrence at Owl Creek Bridge">
        An Occurrence at Owl Creek Bridge
       </a>
       " and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Devil%27s_Dictionary" title="The Devil's Dictionary">
         The Devil's Dictionary
        </a>
       </i>
       , was last heard from in a letter of December 1913 bearing a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Chihuahua,_Chihuahua" title="Chihuahua, Chihuahua">
        Chihuahua
       </a>
       postmark to his secretary and companion, Carrie Christiansen. Although alternative theories are plentiful,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30">
        <a href="#cite_note-30">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         30
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       he almost certainly perished in war-torn Mexico, possibly at the Battle of
       <a href="/wiki/Ojinaga" title="Ojinaga">
        Ojinaga
       </a>
       on 10 February,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-31">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         31
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       or perhaps was executed as a spy in the municipal cemetery of
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Mojada" title="Sierra Mojada">
        Sierra Mojada
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Coahuila" title="Coahuila">
        Coahuila
       </a>
       , where a gravestone bearing his name was erected in 2004.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-32">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         32
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1914 
       <a href="/wiki/F._Lewis_Clark" title="F. Lewis Clark">
        F. Lewis Clark
       </a>
       (52), businessman from the U.S. state of
       <a href="/wiki/Idaho" title="Idaho">
        Idaho
       </a>
       , disappeared while visiting
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara,_California" title="Santa Barbara, California">
        Santa Barbara, California
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1914 
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alejandro_Bello_Silva" title="Alejandro Bello Silva">
        Alejandro Bello Silva
       </a>
       (27), a lieutenant in the
       <a href="/wiki/Chilean_Army" title="Chilean Army">
        Chilean Army
       </a>
       , disappeared during a qualifying examination flight over central
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       . Although search efforts commenced within hours, no trace was ever found. His disappearance is reflected in a Chilean
       <a href="/wiki/Set_phrase" title="Set phrase">
        set phrase
       </a>
       , "more lost than Lieutenant Bello", applied to people who stray off course or disappear en route.
      </li>
      <li>
       1916 
       <a href="/wiki/B%C3%A9la_Kiss" title="Bla Kiss">
        Bla Kiss
       </a>
       (39) was a Hungarian serial killer who murdered 24 young women prior to his enrollment in the Austro-Hungarian Army in the First World War. Upon the discovery of his crimes, he was traced to a Serbian military hospital but escaped a few days before investigators arrived. Although there were several reported sightings of the killer (notably in
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_City" title="New York City">
        New York
       </a>
       in 1932), his true fate remains a mystery.
      </li>
      <li>
       1918 
       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Cravan" title="Arthur Cravan">
        Arthur Cravan
       </a>
       (31), French proto-
       <a href="/wiki/Dada" title="Dada">
        dadaist
       </a>
       writer and art critic, disappeared near
       <a href="/wiki/Salina_Cruz" title="Salina Cruz">
        Salina Cruz
       </a>
       , Mexico; he most likely drowned.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1919 
       <a href="/wiki/Mansell_Richard_James" title="Mansell Richard James">
        Mansell Richard James
       </a>
       (25), a Canadian
       <a href="/wiki/Flying_ace" title="Flying ace">
        flying ace
       </a>
       , was last seen in western Massachusetts on 2 June, just days after a record-setting flight between
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Atlantic_City" title="Atlantic City">
        Atlantic City
       </a>
       and Boston.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33">
        <a href="#cite_note-33">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         33
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1919 
       <a href="/wiki/Ambrose_Small" title="Ambrose Small">
        Ambrose Small
       </a>
       (56), a Canadian millionaire, disappeared from his office. He was last seen at 5:30pm on 2 December 1919, at the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grand_Theatre,_Ontario" title="Grand Theatre, Ontario">
        Grand Theatre
       </a>
       in London, Ontario.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34">
        <a href="#cite_note-34">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         34
         <span>
          ]
         </span>

       </sup>

     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1920s">
       1920s
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 1920s">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       1920 
       <a href="/wiki/Victor_Grayson" title="Victor Grayson">
        Victor Grayson
       </a>
       (39), British socialist politician, received a phone call and told his friends that he had to go to the Queen's Hotel in
       <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Square" title="Leicester Square">
        Leicester Square
       </a>
       and would be back shortly. He was last seen entering a house owned by
       <a href="/wiki/Maundy_Gregory" title="Maundy Gregory">
        Maundy Gregory
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1921  The captain and crew of the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Carroll_A._Deering" title="Carroll A. Deering">
         Carroll A. Deering
        </a>
       </i>
       , which was found beached near Cape Hatteras, North Carolina.
      </li>
      <li>
       1921 
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_White_Whittlesey" title="Charles White Whittlesey">
        Charles Whittlesey
       </a>
       (37), American soldier and
       <a href="/wiki/Medal_of_Honor" title="Medal of Honor">
        Medal of Honor
       </a>
       recipient who led the "
       <a href="/wiki/Lost_Battalion_(World_War_I)" title="Lost Battalion (World War I)">
        Lost Battalion
       </a>
       " in
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">
        World War I
       </a>
       . He was last seen on the evening of 26 November 1921, on a passenger ship bound from New York City to Havana, and is presumed to have committed suicide by jumping overboard.
      </li>
      <li>
       1924 
       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Irvine_(mountaineer)" title="Andrew Irvine (mountaineer)">
        Andrew Irvine
       </a>
       (22), English mountaineer who took part in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/British_Mount_Everest_Expedition_1924" title="British Mount Everest Expedition 1924">
        British Mount Everest Expedition 1924
       </a>
       . He and his climbing partner
       <a href="/wiki/George_Mallory" title="George Mallory">
        George Mallory
       </a>
       disappeared somewhere high on the mountain's northeast ridge. Though Mallory's body was found in 1999, the search for Irvine's continues to this day.
      </li>
      <li>
       1925 
       <a href="/wiki/Percy_Fawcett" title="Percy Fawcett">
        Percy Fawcett
       </a>
       (58), British
       <a href="/wiki/Archaeology" title="Archaeology">
        archaeologist
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/List_of_explorers" title="List of explorers">
        explorer
       </a>
       , together with his eldest son, Jack, and friend Raleigh Rimmell, was last seen travelling into the jungle of
       <a href="/wiki/Mato_Grosso" title="Mato Grosso">
        Mato Grosso
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
        Brazil
       </a>
       to search for a hidden city called the
       <a href="/wiki/Lost_City_of_Z" title="Lost City of Z">
        Lost City of Z
       </a>
       . Several unconfirmed sightings and many conflicting reports and theories explaining their disappearance followed, but despite the loss of over 100 lives in more than a dozen follow-up expeditions and the recovery of some of Fawcett's belongings, their fate remains a mystery.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35">
        <a href="#cite_note-35">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         35
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1925 
       <a href="/wiki/Frederick_McDonald" title="Frederick McDonald">
        Frederick McDonald
       </a>
       , Australian politician, set off from
       <a href="/wiki/Martin_Place,_Sydney" title="Martin Place, Sydney">
        Martin Place, Sydney
       </a>
       , for a meeting with
       <a href="/wiki/Jack_Lang_(Australian_politician)" title="Jack Lang (Australian politician)">
        Jack Lang
       </a>
       two blocks away but failed to arrive. He was possibly murdered by his political rival
       <a href="/wiki/Thomas_Ley" title="Thomas Ley">
        Thomas Ley
       </a>
       . In 1947, Ley was convicted at the
       <a href="/wiki/Old_Bailey" title="Old Bailey">
        Old Bailey
       </a>
       of "the chalkpit murder" of a barman in England and sentenced to hang but was then declared insane and sent to
       <a href="/wiki/Broadmoor_Hospital" title="Broadmoor Hospital">
        Broadmoor
       </a>
       high-security
       <a href="/wiki/Psychiatric_hospital" title="Psychiatric hospital">
        psychiatric hospital
       </a>
       , where he died of a
       <a href="/wiki/Cerebral_hemorrhage" title="Cerebral hemorrhage">
        cerebral hemorrhage
       </a>
       two months later.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36">
        <a href="#cite_note-36">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         36
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1926 
       <a href="/wiki/Agatha_Christie" title="Agatha Christie">
        Agatha Christie
       </a>
       , the British crime writer,
       <a href="/wiki/Agatha_Christie#Disappearance" title="Agatha Christie">
        famously disappeared
       </a>
       . She was located 10 days later in a
       <a href="/wiki/Yorkshire" title="Yorkshire">
        Yorkshire
       </a>
       health spa, and always refused to give an explanation. Subsequent investigations by author Jared Cade have shed considerable light on the event.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37">
        <a href="#cite_note-37">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         37
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1927 
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Nungesser" title="Charles Nungesser">
        Charles Nungesser
       </a>
       (35), French aviator, and his navigator,
       <a href="/wiki/Fran%C3%A7ois_Coli" title="Franois Coli">
        Franois Coli
       </a>
       (45), disappeared while attempting a flight from Paris to New York. They are presumed to have crashed into the Atlantic, or possibly in
       <a href="/wiki/Newfoundland_and_Labrador" title="Newfoundland and Labrador">
        Newfoundland
       </a>
       or
       <a href="/wiki/Maine" title="Maine">
        Maine
       </a>
       , but no wreckage that could be confirmed to be from their biplane,
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_White_Bird" title="The White Bird">
         The White Bird
        </a>
       </i>
       , was ever found.
      </li>
      <li>
       1928 
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Walter_Collins" title="Walter Collins">
        Walter Collins
       </a>
       (9) disappeared from his Los Angeles home.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38">
        <a href="#cite_note-38">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         38
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       His disappearance and the attempt by the Los Angeles police department to convince his mother that a different boy was her son formed the basis of the 2008 film
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Changeling_(film)" title="Changeling (film)">
         Changeling
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1928 
       <a href="/wiki/Glen_and_Bessie_Hyde" title="Glen and Bessie Hyde">
        Glen and Bessie Hyde
       </a>
       (29 &amp; 22), American newlyweds, disappeared while attempting to
       <a href="/wiki/Rafting" title="Rafting">
        raft
       </a>
       the
       <a href="/wiki/Colorado_River" title="Colorado River">
        Colorado River
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Rapid" title="Rapid">
        rapids
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_Canyon" title="Grand Canyon">
        Grand Canyon
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1928 
       <a href="/wiki/Roald_Amundsen" title="Roald Amundsen">
        Roald Amundsen
       </a>
       , Norwegian Arctic explorer and the first man to reach the South Pole, disappeared on a search-and-rescue mission for
       <a href="/wiki/Umberto_Nobile" title="Umberto Nobile">
        Umberto Nobile
       </a>
       and other survivors of the crashed airship
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Airship_Italia" title="Airship Italia">
         Italia
        </a>
        ,
       </i>
       in the Arctic.
      </li>
      <li>
       1928  The Danish sailtraining vessel
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B8benhavn_(ship)" title="Kbenhavn (ship)">
         Kbenhavn
        </a>
       </i>
       ("Copenhagen") vanished en route from Buenos Aires to Australia sometime between December 1928 and January 1929 with the loss of 14 crew and 45 cadets, some of whom were as young as 16years old.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1930s">
       1930s
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 1930s">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       1930  Catherine Moroney, a struggling 17-year-old mother of two, gave her two-year-old daughter
       <a href="/wiki/Mary_Agnes_Moroney" title="Mary Agnes Moroney">
        Mary Agnes
       </a>
       to a stranger calling herself "Julia Otis" in exchange for $2 on May 15, on the understanding that the woman would take care of the girl in California for a short time and then return her to the Moroneys'
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
        Chicago
       </a>
       home when things were better. She never did, and the ensuing investigation attracted national media attention. The girl was never located, and the case remains the oldest unsolved missing-persons case in the city. A California woman's belief that she was Mary Agnes has subsequently been disproven by DNA testing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mary_Agnes_Moroney_39-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Mary_Agnes_Moroney-39">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         39
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1930 
       <a href="/wiki/Joseph_Force_Crater" title="Joseph Force Crater">
        Joseph Force Crater
       </a>
       (41), an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Associate_justice" title="Associate justice">
        associate justice
       </a>
       of the
       <a href="/wiki/New_York_Supreme_Court" title="New York Supreme Court">
        New York Supreme Court
       </a>
       , was last seen on 6 August after a meal at a restaurant. Judge Crater was never seen or heard from again. (His
       <a href="/wiki/Mistress_(lover)" title="Mistress (lover)">
        mistress
       </a>
       , Sally Lou Ritz (22), was falsely said to have disappeared a few weeks later, but was interviewed by police as late as July 1937.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40">
        <a href="#cite_note-40">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         40
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       ) Crater's disappearance, which prompted one of the most sensational manhunts of the 20th century,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41">
        <a href="#cite_note-41">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         41
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       was the subject of widespread media attention and a
       <a href="/wiki/Grand_jury" title="Grand jury">
        grand jury
       </a>
       investigation. Crater was
       <a href="/wiki/Declared_death_in_absentia" title="Declared death in absentia">
        declared legally dead
       </a>
       in 1939 and his missing persons file was officially closed in 1979; however,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cold_case_(criminology)" title="Cold case (criminology)">
        cold case squad
       </a>
       detectives have investigated new leads as recently as 2005.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42">
        <a href="#cite_note-42">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         42
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       To "pull a Crater" became
       <a href="/wiki/Slang" title="Slang">
        slang
       </a>
       for a person vanishing.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43">
        <a href="#cite_note-43">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         43
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1933 
       <a href="/wiki/C._B._Johnston" title="C. B. Johnston">
        C. B. Johnston
       </a>
       (c. 38), American college athlete and coach.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44">
        <a href="#cite_note-44">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         44
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1934 
       <a href="/wiki/Wallace_Fard_Muhammad" title="Wallace Fard Muhammad">
        Wallace Fard Muhammad
       </a>
       (43), founder of the
       <a href="/wiki/Nation_of_Islam" title="Nation of Islam">
        Nation of Islam
       </a>
       , left
       <a href="/wiki/Detroit" title="Detroit">
        Detroit
       </a>
       and was never heard from again.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45">
        <a href="#cite_note-45">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         45
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1934 
       <a href="/wiki/Everett_Ruess" title="Everett Ruess">
        Everett Ruess
       </a>
       (20), a young American artist, disappeared while travelling through the deserts of
       <a href="/wiki/Utah" title="Utah">
        Utah
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1935 
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Kingsford_Smith" title="Charles Kingsford Smith">
        Charles Kingsford Smith
       </a>
       (38), Australian pioneer
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aviator" title="Aviator">
        aviator
       </a>
       , and co-pilot Tommy Pethybridge disappeared during an overnight flight from
       <a href="/wiki/Allahabad" title="Allahabad">
        Allahabad
       </a>
       , India, to
       <a href="/wiki/Singapore" title="Singapore">
        Singapore
       </a>
       while attempting to break the EnglandAustralia speed record. Eighteen months later, Burmese fishermen found an undercarriage leg and wheel (with its tire still inflated) on the shoreline of Aye Island in the
       <a href="/wiki/Andaman_Sea" title="Andaman Sea">
        Andaman Sea
       </a>
       , 3km (2mi) off the southeast coastline of Burma, which
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Corporation" title="Lockheed Corporation">
        Lockheed
       </a>
       confirmed to be from their
       <a href="/wiki/Lockheed_Altair" title="Lockheed Altair">
        Lockheed Altair
       </a>
       , the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Lady_Southern_Cross" title="Lady Southern Cross">
         Lady Southern Cross
        </a>
       </i>
       . Botanists who examined the weeds clinging to it estimated that the aircraft itself lies not far from the island at a depth of approximately 15 fathoms (90ft; 27m).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46">
        <a href="#cite_note-46">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         46
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       A filmmaker claimed to have located
       <i>
        Lady Southern Cross
       </i>
       on the seabed in February 2009.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47">
        <a href="#cite_note-47">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         47
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1937 
       <a href="/wiki/Amelia_Earhart" title="Amelia Earhart">
        Amelia Earhart
       </a>
       (39), famous American
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Aviatrix" title="Aviatrix">
        aviatrix
       </a>
       ; she was the first woman to try a
       <a href="/wiki/Circumnavigation" title="Circumnavigation">
        circumnavigational
       </a>
       flight of the globe. During the attempt she and her
       <a href="/wiki/Navigator" title="Navigator">
        navigator
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Fred_Noonan" title="Fred Noonan">
        Fred Noonan
       </a>
       (44), disappeared over the central Pacific in the vicinity of
       <a href="/wiki/Howland_Island" title="Howland Island">
        Howland Island
       </a>
       , 2 July.
      </li>
      <li>
       1937 
       <a href="/wiki/Sigizmund_Levanevsky" title="Sigizmund Levanevsky">
        Sigizmund Levanevsky
       </a>
       (35), famous
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/USSR" title="USSR">
        Soviet
       </a>
       aviator, together with his crew of five and their
       <a href="/wiki/Bolkhovitinov_DB-A" title="Bolkhovitinov DB-A">
        Bolkhovitinov DB-A
       </a>
       aircraft, disappeared in the vicinity of the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Pole" title="North Pole">
        North Pole
       </a>
       after reporting loss of power from one of their four
       <a href="/wiki/Mikulin_AM-34" title="Mikulin AM-34">
        Mikulin AM-34
       </a>
       engines while attempting to prove a trans
       <a href="/wiki/Polar_route" title="Polar route">
        polar route
       </a>
       between
       <a href="/wiki/Asia" title="Asia">
        Asia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/North_America" title="North America">
        North America
       </a>
       commercially viable.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48">
        <a href="#cite_note-48">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         48
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1937 
       <a href="/wiki/Juliet_Stuart_Poyntz" title="Juliet Stuart Poyntz">
        Juliet Stuart Poyntz
       </a>
       (50), was a member of the Daughters of the American Revolution (DAR), and a founding member of the Communist Party of the United States (CPUSA). After resigning from active work with the Party, she disappeared in 1937, never to be seen again. She is believed by several sources to have been abducted and murdered by a Soviet NKVD assassination squad.
      </li>
      <li>
       1937 
       <a href="/wiki/Theodore_Cole_and_Ralph_Roe" title="Theodore Cole and Ralph Roe">
        Theodore Cole and Ralph Roe
       </a>
       (24 &amp; 28) escaped from
       <a href="/wiki/Alcatraz_Island" title="Alcatraz Island">
        Alcatraz prison
       </a>
       in the U.S. state of
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       and disappeared. Authorities presumed that they drowned, but no bodies were ever recovered.
      </li>
      <li>
       1938 
       <a href="/wiki/Ettore_Majorana" title="Ettore Majorana">
        Ettore Majorana
       </a>
       (31), Italian physicist, disappeared during a boat trip from
       <a href="/wiki/Naples" title="Naples">
        Naples
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Palermo" title="Palermo">
        Palermo
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1938 
       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie_Whitfield" title="Andrew Carnegie Whitfield">
        Andrew Carnegie Whitfield
       </a>
       (28), nephew of U.S. steel magnate
       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Carnegie" title="Andrew Carnegie">
        Andrew Carnegie
       </a>
       , disappeared during a solo morning flight in a small
       <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Cub" title="Taylor Cub">
        Taylor Cub
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Light_aircraft" title="Light aircraft">
        light aircraft
       </a>
       from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Roosevelt_Field,_New_York" title="Roosevelt Field, New York">
        Roosevelt Field, New York
       </a>
       , on
       <a href="/wiki/Long_Island" title="Long Island">
        Long Island
       </a>
       to an airfield at
       <a href="/wiki/Brentwood,_New_York" title="Brentwood, New York">
        Brentwood
       </a>
       , approximately 22miles away.
      </li>
      <li>
       1938 
       <a href="/wiki/Willie_McLean_(American_soccer)" title="Willie McLean (American soccer)">
        Willie McLean
       </a>
       (34), an American soccer player who played in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/1934_World_Cup" title="1934 World Cup">
        1934 World Cup
       </a>
       . His family received occasional Mother's Day cards for several years afterwards, purportedly from McLean.
      </li>
      <li>
       1939 
       <a href="/wiki/Barbara_Newhall_Follett" title="Barbara Newhall Follett">
        Barbara Newhall Follett
       </a>
       (25) was an American child prodigy novelist. Her first novel,
       <i>
        The House Without Windows
       </i>
       , was published in 1927 when she was twelve years old. Her next novel,
       <i>
        The Voyage of the Norman D.
       </i>
       , received critical acclaim when she was fourteen. In 1939, aged 25, she became depressed with her marriage and walked out of her apartment with just thirty dollars. She was never seen again.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49">
        <a href="#cite_note-49">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         49
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1939 
       <a href="/wiki/Lloyd_L._Gaines" title="Lloyd L. Gaines">
        Lloyd L. Gaines
       </a>
       (28) was the central figure in
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Missouri_ex_rel._Gaines_v._Canada" title="Missouri ex rel. Gaines v. Canada">
         Missouri ex rel. Gaines v. Canada
        </a>
       </i>
       , an early success for the
       <a href="/wiki/African-American_Civil_Rights_Movement_(1896%E2%80%931954)" title="African-American Civil Rights Movement (18961954)">
        U.S. civil rights movement
       </a>
       . One evening, he left his
       <a href="/wiki/Alpha_Phi_Alpha" title="Alpha Phi Alpha">
        Alpha Phi Alpha
       </a>
       fraternity house in
       <a href="/wiki/Chicago" title="Chicago">
        Chicago
       </a>
       , having told the housekeeper he was going to buy some stamps, and was never seen or heard from again. Some accounts suggest he was living in New York or Mexico City in the late 1940s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Riverfront_Times_story_50-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Riverfront_Times_story-50">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         50
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1939 
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Halliburton" title="Richard Halliburton">
        Richard Halliburton
       </a>
       , missing at sea since March 1939 after trying to sail
       <i>
        Sea Dragon
       </i>
       (a gaudily decorated, 75-foot Chinese
       <a href="/wiki/Junk_(ship)" title="Junk (ship)">
        junk
       </a>
       ) across the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       . In 1945, some wreckage identified as a rudder and believed to belong to the
       <i>
        Sea Dragon
       </i>
       washed ashore in
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1939 
       <a href="/wiki/Rita_Gorgonowa" title="Rita Gorgonowa">
        Rita Gorgonowa
       </a>
       (38), defendant in a widely publicized 1931 Polish murder trial where she had been convicted of murdering a child under her care while employed as a governess, was released from prison after a successful appeal on 3 September, a date moved up due to the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/German_invasion_of_Poland" title="German invasion of Poland">
        German invasion
       </a>
       that started
       <a href="/wiki/World_War_II" title="World War II">
        World War II
       </a>
       in Europe two days earlier. Her subsequent whereabouts are unknown. Her children say she survived the war; she was reported to have either remained in Poland under an assumed name or emigrated to South America and lived out her life there.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1940s">
       1940s
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 1940s">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1942">
       1942
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 1942">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       The later whereabouts of
       <a href="/wiki/James_Litterick" title="James Litterick">
        James Litterick
       </a>
       , 41, first
       <a href="/wiki/Communist_Party_of_Canada" title="Communist Party of Canada">
        Communist
       </a>
       elected to the
       <a href="/wiki/Manitoba" title="Manitoba">
        Manitoba
       </a>
       provincial parliament, are unknown following his release from police custody (he had been at large since the Communist Party was banned in 1940). One report has him working at a Toronto garment factory the following year.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1944">
       1944
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1944">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Glenn_Miller" title="Glenn Miller">
        Glenn Miller
       </a>
       (40), the popular American
       <a href="/wiki/Jazz" title="Jazz">
        jazz
       </a>
       musician and
       <a href="/wiki/Bandleader" title="Bandleader">
        bandleader
       </a>
       , was en route from England to France on 15 December 1944, to play for troops in recently liberated Paris when the single-engined
       <a href="/wiki/Noorduyn_Norseman" title="Noorduyn Norseman">
        Noorduyn Norseman
       </a>
       aircraft in which he was a passenger disappeared over the
       <a href="/wiki/English_Channel" title="English Channel">
        English Channel
       </a>
