       . The plane and those on board have never been located. As a U.S. military officer who vanished in wartime, Miller continues to be listed officially as
       <a href="/wiki/Missing_in_action" title="Missing in action">
        missing in action
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Rocco_Perri" title="Rocco Perri">
        Rocco Perri
       </a>
       (born 30 December 1887, last seen alive 23 April 1944) was an organized crime figure in Ontario, Canada, in the early 20th century.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Szilveszter_Matuska" title="Szilveszter Matuska">
        Szilveszter Matuska
       </a>
       , Hungarian mass-murderer known as "The Train Killer", escaped from jail in 1944 and was never recaptured.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Herschel_Grynszpan" title="Herschel Grynszpan">
        Herschel Grynszpan
       </a>
       (22), Jewish exile from Germany whose 1938 assassination of diplomat
       <a href="/wiki/Ernst_vom_Rath" title="Ernst vom Rath">
        Ernst vom Rath
       </a>
       in Paris was the trigger for
       <a href="/wiki/Kristallnacht" title="Kristallnacht">
        Kristallnacht
       </a>
       . For various reasons, largely legal delays, a planned trial was never held in either France or (after 1940) Germany, while Grynszpan was held in various prisons and concentration camps.
       <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Eichmann" title="Adolf Eichmann">
        Adolf Eichmann
       </a>
       testified at his 1961 trial in Jerusalem that he had interrogated Grynszpan in
       <a href="/wiki/Magdeburg" title="Magdeburg">
        Magdeburg
       </a>
       in either late 1943 or early 1944; after that there is no record of his whereabouts or ultimate fate. The West German government had him declared legally dead in 1960.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Herschel_Grynszpan_51-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Herschel_Grynszpan-51">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         51
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Antoine_de_Saint-Exup%C3%A9ry" title="Antoine de Saint-Exupry">
        Antoine de Saint-Exupry
       </a>
       (44), French author and aviator, last seen when flying a reconnaissance mission out of Corsica in preparation for the Allied invasion of Southern France. The remains of his aircraft, found at sea off Marseille, would be identified in 2004.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1945">
       1945
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 1945">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Heinrich_M%C3%BCller_(Gestapo)" title="Heinrich Mller (Gestapo)">
        Heinrich Mller
       </a>
       (45),
       <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">
        Nazi
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Gestapo" title="Gestapo">
        Gestapo
       </a>
       chief, last confirmed sighting in the
       <a href="/wiki/F%C3%BChrerbunker" title="Fhrerbunker">
        Fhrerbunker
       </a>
       on the evening of 1 May 1945. His
       <a href="/wiki/Central_Intelligence_Agency" title="Central Intelligence Agency">
        CIA
       </a>
       file and related documents state that while the record is "...inconclusive on Mller's ultimate fate... [he] most likely died in Berlin in early May 1945."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-52">
        <a href="#cite_note-52">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         52
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Raoul_Wallenberg" title="Raoul Wallenberg">
        Raoul Wallenberg
       </a>
       (32), Swedish diplomat credited with saving the lives of at least 20,000 Hungarian Jews during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Holocaust" title="Holocaust">
        Holocaust
       </a>
       , was arrested on espionage charges in Budapest following the arrival of the Soviet army. His subsequent fate remains a mystery despite hundreds of purported sightings in Soviet prisons, some as recent as the 1980s. In 2001, after 10 years of research, a Swedish-Russian panel concluded that Wallenberg probably died or was executed in Soviet custody on 17 July 1947, but to date no hard evidence has been found to confirm this.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53">
        <a href="#cite_note-53">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         53
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In 2010, evidence from Russian archives surfaced suggesting he was alive after the presumed execution date.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54">
        <a href="#cite_note-54">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         54
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Constanze_Manziarly" title="Constanze Manziarly">
        Constanze Manziarly
       </a>
       (25), cook and dietitian to
       <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">
        Adolf Hitler
       </a>
       , disappeared while escaping
       <a href="/wiki/Berlin" title="Berlin">
        Berlin
       </a>
       following the
       <a href="/wiki/Battle_of_Berlin" title="Battle of Berlin">
        Soviet invasion
       </a>
       and fall of
       <a href="/wiki/Nazi_Germany" title="Nazi Germany">
        Nazi Germany
       </a>
       . She was believed to have been shot by
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet
       </a>
       soldiers in an
       <a href="/wiki/Berlin_U-Bahn" title="Berlin U-Bahn">
        U-Bahn subway
       </a>
       tunnel.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55">
        <a href="#cite_note-55">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         55
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Alfred_Partikel" title="Alfred Partikel">
        Alfred Partikel
       </a>
       (57), German painter of
       <a href="/wiki/East_Prussia" title="East Prussia">
        East Prussian
       </a>
       origin, vanished while picking mushrooms in the woods near the artist's colony of
       <a href="/wiki/Ahrenshoop" title="Ahrenshoop">
        Ahrenshoop
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Dar%C3%9F" title="Dar">
        Dar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Western_Pomerania" title="Western Pomerania">
        Western Pomerania
       </a>
       . His remains have never been found.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Supriyadi" title="Supriyadi">
        Supriyadi
       </a>
       (22) was an Indonesian national hero. On 6 October 1945, in a government decree issued by the newly independent
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </a>
       , Supriyadi was named Minister for Public Security in the first cabinet. However, he failed to appear and was replaced on 20 October by ad interim minister Muhammad Soeljoadikusuma. To this day his fate remains unknown.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SUDARMANTO2312_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SUDARMANTO2312-56">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         56
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-SIMANJUNTAK18_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-SIMANJUNTAK18-57">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         57
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Genrikh_Lyushkov" title="Genrikh Lyushkov">
        Genrikh Lyushkov
       </a>
       (45), high-level
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_Union" title="Soviet Union">
        Soviet
       </a>
       defector and former
       <a href="/wiki/Russian_Far_East" title="Russian Far East">
        Far East
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/NKVD" title="NKVD">
        NKVD
       </a>
       chief. A participant in the
       <a href="/wiki/Great_Purge" title="Great Purge">
        Great Purge
       </a>
       , he fled to avoid what he believed would be arrest and execution into the
       <a href="/wiki/Japan" title="Japan">
        Japanese
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Puppet_state" title="Puppet state">
        puppet state
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Manchukuo" title="Manchukuo">
        Manchukuo
       </a>
       . After his defection, he became a military consultant and analyst for the
       <a href="/wiki/Imperial_Japanese_Army" title="Imperial Japanese Army">
        Imperial Japanese Army
       </a>
       . He disappeared during the
       <a href="/wiki/Soviet_invasion_of_Manchuria" title="Soviet invasion of Manchuria">
        Soviet invasion of Manchuria
       </a>
       and was reported as being last seen in a crowded train station in Dairen (
       <a href="/wiki/Dalian" title="Dalian">
        Dalian
       </a>
       ). Several theories exist about his fate, but he is presumed to have died in 1945, killed either by Soviet or Japanese forces.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58">
        <a href="#cite_note-58">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         58
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1946">
       1946
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 1946">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Paula_Jean_Welden" title="Paula Jean Welden">
        Paula Jean Welden
       </a>
       (18),
       <a href="/wiki/Bennington_College" title="Bennington College">
        Bennington College
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sophomore_year" title="Sophomore year">
        sophomore
       </a>
       , disappeared while walking on the
       <a href="/wiki/Long_Trail" title="Long Trail">
        Long Trail
       </a>
       near
       <a href="/wiki/Glastenbury_Mountain" title="Glastenbury Mountain">
        Glastenbury Mountain
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Vermont" title="Vermont">
        Vermont
       </a>
       , USA.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59">
        <a href="#cite_note-59">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         59
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60">
        <a href="#cite_note-60">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         60
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1947">
       1947
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: 1947">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       In the aftermath of the
       <a href="/wiki/1947_Glazier%E2%80%93Higgins%E2%80%93Woodward_tornadoes" title="1947 GlazierHigginsWoodward tornadoes">
        1947 GlazierHigginsWoodward tornadoes
       </a>
       , 4-year-old Joan Gay Croft and her sister Jerri were among refugees taking shelter in a basement hallway of the Woodward hospital. As officials sent the injured to different hospitals in the area, two men took Joan away, saying they were taking her to Oklahoma City. She was never seen again. Over the years, several women have come forth saying they suspect they might be Joan. None of their claims have been verified.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61">
        <a href="#cite_note-61">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         61
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62">
        <a href="#cite_note-62">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         62
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1948">
       1948
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: 1948">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Arthur_Coningham_(RAF_officer)" title="Arthur Coningham (RAF officer)">
        Sir Arthur Coningham
       </a>
       (53), retired
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Air_Force" title="Royal Air Force">
        RAF
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Air_Marshal" title="Air Marshal">
        Air Marshal
       </a>
       , disappeared when
       <a href="/wiki/Avro_Tudor" title="Avro Tudor">
        Avro Tudor IV
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G-AHNP_%22Star_Tiger%22" title='G-AHNP "Star Tiger"'>
        G-AHNP
        <i>
         Star Tiger
        </i>
       </a>
       went missing over the western Atlantic.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63">
        <a href="#cite_note-63">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         63
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       He was one of 25passengers, together with six crewmen, who were lost when the flight from
       <a href="/wiki/Santa_Maria_Airport_(Azores)" title="Santa Maria Airport (Azores)">
        Santa Maria Airport
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Azores" title="Azores">
        Azores
       </a>
       failed to reach its destination of
       <a href="/wiki/Kindley_Air_Force_Base" title="Kindley Air Force Base">
        Kindley Field
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Bermuda" title="Bermuda">
        Bermuda
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64">
        <a href="#cite_note-64">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         64
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <i>
        Star Tiger'
       </i>
       s sister aircraft
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/G-AGRE_%22Star_Ariel%22" title='G-AGRE "Star Ariel"'>
        G-AGRE
        <i>
         Star Ariel
        </i>
       </a>
       also disappeared over the western Atlantic, with the loss of all seven crewmen and 13 passengers, while flying from Bermuda to
       <a href="/wiki/Norman_Manley_International_Airport" title="Norman Manley International Airport">
        Kingston Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jamaica" title="Jamaica">
        Jamaica
       </a>
       , the following year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65">
        <a href="#cite_note-65">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         65
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Virginia_Carpenter" title="Disappearance of Virginia Carpenter">
        Virginia Carpenter
       </a>
       (21), was last seen talking to the occupants of a car parked in front of her dorm at the Texas State College for Women in
       <a href="/wiki/Denton,_Texas" title="Denton, Texas">
        Denton
       </a>
       on 1 June 1948. Many sightings were reported in the days afterwards, but she was never found nor has any evidence of her fate come to light.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1949">
       1949
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: 1949">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Jean_Spangler" title="Jean Spangler">
        Jean Spangler
       </a>
       (26), American dancer, model and bit-part actress, disappeared in October 1949 from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Los_Angeles,_California" title="Los Angeles, California">
        Los Angeles, California
       </a>
       . Last seen by her sister-in-law before going to meet her ex-husband. Two days later her purse was found near the entrance gate to
       <a href="/wiki/Griffith_Park" title="Griffith Park">
        Griffith Park
       </a>
       in Los Angeles.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1950s">
       1950s
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: 1950s">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       1950 
       <a href="/wiki/Richard_Colvin_Cox" title="Richard Colvin Cox">
        Richard Colvin Cox
       </a>
       (20), second-year military cadet, disappeared from the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Military_Academy" title="United States Military Academy">
        United States Military Academy
       </a>
       at
       <a href="/wiki/West_Point,_New_York" title="West Point, New York">
        West Point, New York
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1951 
       <a href="/wiki/Vincent_Mangano" title="Vincent Mangano">
        Vincent Mangano
       </a>
       (63),
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Crime_boss" title="Crime boss">
        crime boss
       </a>
       of the future
       <a href="/wiki/Gambino_crime_family" title="Gambino crime family">
        Gambino crime family
       </a>
       , disappeared on the same day that his brother,
       <a href="/wiki/Philip_Mangano" title="Philip Mangano">
        Philip Mangano
       </a>
       , was found murdered. He is believed to have been killed on the orders of
       <a href="/wiki/Albert_Anastasia" title="Albert Anastasia">
        Albert Anastasia
       </a>
       as part of a coup.
      </li>
      <li>
       1951 
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Beverly_Potts" title="Beverly Potts">
        Beverly Potts
       </a>
       (10), American schoolgirl from
       <a href="/wiki/Cleveland" title="Cleveland">
        Cleveland
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ohio" title="Ohio">
        Ohio
       </a>
       , disappeared while walking home from an entertainment event at Halloran Park. She is believed by police to have been abducted and murdered, possibly by someone she knew and trusted as she was shy and fearful of strangers.
      </li>
      <li>
       1953 
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/First_Lieutenant" title="First Lieutenant">
        First Lieutenant
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Felix_Moncla" title="Felix Moncla">
        Felix Moncla
       </a>
       (27), pilot, and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Second_Lieutenant" title="Second Lieutenant">
        Second Lieutenant
       </a>
       Robert Wilson (22), radar operator, disappeared when their
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">
        United States Air Force
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/F-89_Scorpion" title="F-89 Scorpion">
        F-89 Scorpion
       </a>
       was scrambled from
       <a href="/wiki/Kincheloe_Air_Force_Base" title="Kincheloe Air Force Base">
        Kincheloe Air Force Base
       </a>
       and subsequently went missing over
       <a href="/wiki/Lake_Superior" title="Lake Superior">
        Lake Superior
       </a>
       while intercepting an unknown aircraft in
       <a href="/wiki/Canadian_airspace" title="Canadian airspace">
        Canadian airspace
       </a>
       close to the
       <a href="/wiki/Canada%E2%80%93United_States_border" title="CanadaUnited States border">
        CanadaUnited States border
       </a>
       . The USAF claimed the second aircraft was
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Canadian_Air_Force" title="Royal Canadian Air Force">
        Royal Canadian Air Force
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/C-47_Skytrain" title="C-47 Skytrain">
        C-47 Dakota
       </a>
       VC-912, crossing Northern Lake Superior from west to east at 7,000 feet en route from
       <a href="/wiki/Winnipeg" title="Winnipeg">
        Winnipeg
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Greater_Sudbury" title="Greater Sudbury">
        Sudbury
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Canada" title="Canada">
        Canada
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66">
        <a href="#cite_note-66">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         66
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       The RCAF stated it had no record of such an incident.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67">
        <a href="#cite_note-67">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         67
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Some
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Ufologists" title="Ufologists">
        ufologists
       </a>
       have associated the disappearance with alleged "
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/UFO" title="UFO">
        UFO
       </a>
       " activity and refer to it as the "
       <a href="/wiki/Felix_Moncla" title="Felix Moncla">
        Kinross Incident
       </a>
       ".
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68">
        <a href="#cite_note-68">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         68
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1953 
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Henry_Borynski" title="Disappearance of Henry Borynski">
        Henry Borynski
       </a>
       , a Polish Catholic priest and outspoken anti-Communist, disappeared in Bradford, Yorkshire.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BBC2_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-BBC2-69">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         69
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1955  The crew and passengers of the 69-foot merchant vessel
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/MV_Joyita" title="MV Joyita">
         Joyita
        </a>
       </i>
       , which disappeared in the South Pacific; the
       <i>
        Joyita
       </i>
       was found five weeks later, partially submerged and listing heavily, with no one on board.
      </li>
      <li>
       1955 
       <a href="/wiki/Weldon_Kees" title="Weldon Kees">
        Weldon Kees
       </a>
       (41), U.S. poet, disappeared without leaving a note but had talked about packing up and moving to Mexico. His Plymouth Savoy was found on the north side of the
       <a href="/wiki/Golden_Gate_Bridge" title="Golden Gate Bridge">
        Golden Gate Bridge
       </a>
       with the keys in the ignition.
      </li>
      <li>
       1955 
       <a href="/wiki/Curtis_Chillingworth" title="Curtis Chillingworth">
        Curtis Chillingworth
       </a>
       (58), was a Florida attorney and state judge who disappeared from his Manalapan, Florida home, and was later murdered along with his wife, Marjorie Chillingworth (56).
      </li>
      <li>
       1956  Three
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Air_Force" title="United States Air Force">
        United States Air Force
       </a>
       airmen, commander Captain Robert H. Hodgin (31), observer Captain Gordon M. Insley (32), and pilot 2nd Lt. Ronald L. Kurtz (22), disappeared when their
       <a href="/wiki/1956_B-47_disappearance" title="1956 B-47 disappearance">
        B-47 Stratojet was lost
       </a>
       after failing to make contact with an
       <a href="/wiki/Aerial_refueling" title="Aerial refueling">
        aerial refueling
       </a>
       tanker at 14,000ft over the Mediterranean.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70">
        <a href="#cite_note-70">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         70
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1956 
       <a href="/wiki/Lionel_Crabb" title="Lionel Crabb">
        Lionel "Buster" Crabb
       </a>
       (46), retired British
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Navy" title="Royal Navy">
        Royal Navy
       </a>
       <a href="/wiki/Frogman" title="Frogman">
        frogman
       </a>
       , disappeared during an
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/MI6" title="MI6">
        MI6
       </a>
       mission to spy on the Soviet
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sverdlov_class_cruiser" title="Sverdlov class cruiser">
        <i>
         Sverdlov
        </i>
        class cruiser
       </a>
       <i>
        Ordzhonikidze
       </i>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Portsmouth_Harbour" title="Portsmouth Harbour">
        Portsmouth Harbour
       </a>
       . The coroner concluded that a body (missing its head and hands) in a frogman suit found floating in
       <a href="/wiki/Chichester_Harbour" title="Chichester Harbour">
        Chichester Harbour
       </a>
       the following year was Crabb's, but no positive identification was ever made nor cause of death determined.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71">
        <a href="#cite_note-71">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         71
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1956 
       <a href="/wiki/Gunnel_Gummeson" title="Gunnel Gummeson">
        Gunnel Gummeson
       </a>
       (26), Swedish teacher, disappeared with her American boyfriend, Peter Winant, travelling in
       <a href="/wiki/Afghanistan" title="Afghanistan">
        Afghanistan
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1957 
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moira_McCall_Anderson" title="Moira McCall Anderson">
        Moira McCall Anderson
       </a>
       (11) disappeared while on an errand for her
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Grandmother" title="Grandmother">
        grandmother
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Coatbridge" title="Coatbridge">
        Coatbridge
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Lanarkshire" title="Lanarkshire">
        Lanarkshire
       </a>
       , Scotland. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Moira_Anderson_Foundation" title="Moira Anderson Foundation">
        Moira Anderson Foundation
       </a>
       was established in memory of her.
      </li>
      <li>
       1957 
       <a href="/wiki/Maud_Crawford" title="Maud Crawford">
        Maud Crawford
       </a>
       (63), was the first woman attorney in Camden, Arkansas; her disappearance and presumed death sparked attention for more than three decades. The case remains officially unsolved.
      </li>
      <li>
       1959 
       <a href="/wiki/Camilo_Cienfuegos" title="Camilo Cienfuegos">
        Camilo Cienfuegos
       </a>
       (27),
       <a href="/wiki/Cuba" title="Cuba">
        Cuban
       </a>
       revolutionary and friend of
       <a href="/wiki/Fidel_Castro" title="Fidel Castro">
        Fidel Castro
       </a>
       , disappeared when his
       <a href="/wiki/Cessna_310" title="Cessna 310">
        Cessna 310
       </a>
       went missing over the ocean during a night flight from
       <a href="/wiki/Camag%C3%BCey" title="Camagey">
        Camagey
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Havana" title="Havana">
        Havana
       </a>
       .
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1960s">
       1960s
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: 1960s">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <ul>
      <li>
       1960 
       <a href="/wiki/James_Squillante" title="James Squillante">
        James Squillante
       </a>
       (41), a
       <a href="/wiki/Caporegime" title="Caporegime">
        caporegime
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Gambino_crime_family" title="Gambino crime family">
        Gambino crime family
       </a>
       , disappeared after being indicted on
       <a href="/wiki/Extortion" title="Extortion">
        extortion
       </a>
       charges. He is believed to have been murdered and his body disposed of in a
       <a href="/wiki/Car_crusher" title="Car crusher">
        car crusher
       </a>
       and subsequently melted down in an
       <a href="/wiki/Open_hearth_furnace" title="Open hearth furnace">
        open hearth furnace
       </a>
       , although no physical evidence has ever been found to substantiate this and no one was ever charged for the crime.
      </li>
      <li>
       1961 
       <a href="/wiki/Michael_Rockefeller" title="Michael Rockefeller">
        Michael Rockefeller
       </a>
       (23), son of
       <a href="/wiki/Nelson_Rockefeller" title="Nelson Rockefeller">
        Nelson Rockefeller
       </a>
       , disappeared during an expedition in the
       <a href="/wiki/Asmat_people" title="Asmat people">
        Asmat
       </a>
       region of southwestern
       <a href="/wiki/New_Guinea" title="New Guinea">
        New Guinea
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1961 
       <a href="/wiki/David_Kenyon_Webster" title="David Kenyon Webster">
        David Kenyon Webster
       </a>
       (39), a journalist for the
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Daily_News" title="Los Angeles Daily News">
         Los Angeles Daily News
        </a>
        ,
       </i>
       and
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Saturday_Evening_Post" title="The Saturday Evening Post">
         The Saturday Evening Post
        </a>
        ,
       </i>
       and a World War II veteran with "Easy" Company of the 506th Parachute Infantry Regiment, 101st Airborne Division (made famous in the book and miniseries
       <i>
        Band of Brothers
       </i>
       ), went out on a boat near the coast of Santa Monica and disappeared; he is presumed drowned, though no body was ever recovered.
      </li>
      <li>
       1962 
       <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Strollo" title="Anthony Strollo">
        Anthony Strollo
       </a>
       (62), a
       <a href="/wiki/Caporegime" title="Caporegime">
        caporegime
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Genovese_crime_family" title="Genovese crime family">
        Genovese crime family
       </a>
       , last seen leaving his residence in
       <a href="/wiki/Fort_Lee,_New_Jersey" title="Fort Lee, New Jersey">
        Fort Lee, New Jersey
       </a>
       . He is believed to have been murdered on the orders of
       <a href="/wiki/Vito_Genovese" title="Vito Genovese">
        Vito Genovese
       </a>
       in retaliation for having conspired to have Genovese imprisoned for drug trafficking, although no traces of his remains were ever recovered.
      </li>
      <li>
       1962 
       <a href="/wiki/Frank_Morris_(prisoner)" title="Frank Morris (prisoner)">
        Frank Morris
       </a>
       (35) and brothers
       <a href="/wiki/Clarence_Anglin" title="Clarence Anglin">
        Clarence
       </a>
       (31) and
       <a href="/wiki/John_Anglin" title="John Anglin">
        John Anglin
       </a>
       (32)
       <a href="/wiki/June_1962_Alcatraz_escape" title="June 1962 Alcatraz escape">
        escaped
       </a>
       from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alcatraz" title="Alcatraz">
        Alcatraz prison
       </a>
       in the U.S. state of
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       and disappeared. Authorities presumed that they drowned but no bodies were ever found.
      </li>
      <li>
       1964 
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Clifford_Ogle" title="Charles Clifford Ogle">
        Charles Clifford Ogle
       </a>
       (41) took off from
       <a href="/wiki/Oakland_International_Airport" title="Oakland International Airport">
        Oakland International Airport
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">
        California
       </a>
       , in his
       <a href="/wiki/Cessna_210" title="Cessna 210">
        Cessna 210
       </a>
       , a single-engine aircraft, and was never seen again.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2009)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1965 
       <a href="/wiki/Mehdi_Ben_Barka" title="Mehdi Ben Barka">
        Mehdi Ben Barka
       </a>
       (45), a Moroccan politician, disappeared while in exile in Paris.
      </li>
      <li>
       1965 
       <a href="/wiki/Charles_Rogers_(murder_suspect)" title="Charles Rogers (murder suspect)">
        Charles Rogers
       </a>
       (43), a reclusive unemployed
       <a href="/wiki/Seismology" title="Seismology">
        seismologist
       </a>
       in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Houston,_Texas" title="Houston, Texas">
        Houston, Texas
       </a>
       , has remained at large since the "Icebox Murders" of his parents were discovered on June 23, leading to a warrant for his detention as a material witness. It has been theorized that he had worked for the CIA in the past and may have had connections to figures involved in
       <a href="/wiki/John_F._Kennedy_assassination_conspiracy_theories" title="John F. Kennedy assassination conspiracy theories">
        Kennedy assassination conspiracy theories
       </a>
       . He was declared legally dead in 1975.
      </li>
      <li>
       1966 
       <a href="/wiki/Beaumont_children_disappearance" title="Beaumont children disappearance">
        The Beaumont children
       </a>
       , Jane Nartare (9), Arnna Kathleen (7), and Grant Ellis (4), were three siblings who disappeared from a beach near
       <a href="/wiki/Adelaide" title="Adelaide">
        Adelaide
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">
        South Australia
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       1967 
       <a href="/wiki/John_Lake_(journalist)" title="John Lake (journalist)">
        John Lake
       </a>
       (37) was the sports editor of
       <i>
        Newsweek
       </i>
       until his mysterious disappearance in December 1967.
      </li>
      <li>
       1967 
       <a href="/wiki/Jim_Thompson_(designer)" title="Jim Thompson (designer)">
        Jim Thompson
       </a>
       (61), former U.S.
       <a href="/wiki/Military_intelligence" title="Military intelligence">
        military intelligence
       </a>
       officer who once worked for the
       <a href="/wiki/Office_of_Strategic_Services" title="Office of Strategic Services">
        Office of Strategic Services
       </a>
       (and later known as the "Thai Silk King" for his revival of the
       <a href="/wiki/Thai_silk" title="Thai silk">
        Thai silk
       </a>
       industry), failed to return from an afternoon walk in the
       <a href="/wiki/Cameron_Highlands" title="Cameron Highlands">
        Cameron Highlands
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Pahang" title="Pahang">
        Pahang
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Malaysia" title="Malaysia">
        Malaysia
       </a>
       , quickly prompting a massive manhunt. Many have since investigated his disappearance and attempted to explain it, but no trace of him has ever been found.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72">
        <a href="#cite_note-72">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         72
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1967 
       <a href="/wiki/James_P._Brady" title="James P. Brady">
        James P. Brady
       </a>
       (59), Canadian
       <a href="/wiki/M%C3%A9tis_people_(Canada)" title="Mtis people (Canada)">
        Metis
       </a>
       leader, and a
       <a href="/wiki/Cree" title="Cree">
        Cree
       </a>
       friend, Abraham Halkett (40), disappeared while on a prospecting trip in northern
       <a href="/wiki/Saskatchewan" title="Saskatchewan">
        Saskatchewan
       </a>
       . An extensive land, air, and water search located their camp but failed to find any trace of either man.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         73
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1967 
       <a href="/wiki/Harold_Holt" title="Harold Holt">
        Harold Holt
       </a>
       (59), then
       <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Australia" title="Prime Minister of Australia">
        Prime Minister of Australia
       </a>
       , disappeared while swimming in heavy surf at a beach notorious for strong and dangerous rip currents. Despite one of the largest
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Search-and-rescue" title="Search-and-rescue">
        search-and-rescue
       </a>
       operations ever mounted in Australia, his body was never found.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74">
        <a href="#cite_note-74">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         74
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-75">
        <a href="#cite_note-75">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         75
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       1969 
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/April_Fabb" title="April Fabb">
        April Fabb
       </a>
       (13) went missing in mysterious circumstances from Metton,
       <a href="/wiki/Norfolk" title="Norfolk">
        Norfolk
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom" title="United Kingdom">
        United Kingdom
       </a>
       .
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1970s">
       1970s
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: 1970s">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1970">
       1970
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: 1970">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Verg%C3%A8s" title="Jacques Vergs">
        Jacques Vergs
       </a>
       , a French-Vietnamese lawyer, left his wife
       <a href="/wiki/Djamila_Bouhired" title="Djamila Bouhired">
        Djamila Bouhired
       </a>
       and cut off all ties. He was
       <a href="/wiki/Jacques_Verg%C3%A8s#Missing_years" title="Jacques Vergs">
        last seen
       </a>
       on 24 February 1970, until he reappeared in 1978, without ever explaining his whereabouts during that period.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Sean_Flynn_(photojournalist)" title="Sean Flynn (photojournalist)">
        Sean Flynn
       </a>
       (28), son of
       <a href="/wiki/Errol_Flynn" title="Errol Flynn">
        Errol Flynn
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Lili_Damita" title="Lili Damita">
        Lili Damita
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Dana_Stone" title="Dana Stone">
        Dana Stone
       </a>
       (32), American
       <a href="/wiki/Photojournalism" title="Photojournalism">
        photojournalists
       </a>
       on assignment for
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Time_(magazine)" title="Time (magazine)">
         Time Magazine
        </a>
       </i>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/CBS" title="CBS">
        CBS
       </a>
       News, respectively, were captured by Communist guerrillas while travelling by motorcycle in
       <a href="/wiki/Cambodia" title="Cambodia">
        Cambodia
       </a>
       , 6 April.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Robin_Graham" title="Disappearance of Robin Graham">
        Robin Graham
       </a>
       (18), ran out of gas on the
       <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Freeway" title="Hollywood Freeway">
        Hollywood Freeway
       </a>
       . She was last seen by
       <a href="/wiki/California_Highway_Patrol" title="California Highway Patrol">
        California Highway Patrol
       </a>
       (CHP) officers, who directed her to a
       <a href="/wiki/Callbox" title="Callbox">
        callbox
       </a>
       and later saw her speaking with a man beside her car. The circumstances of her disappearance resulted in CHP policies being changed to ensure the safety of stranded female motorists.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76">
        <a href="#cite_note-76">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         76
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1971">
       1971
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: 1971">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       The unidentified
       <a href="/wiki/Aircraft_hijacking" title="Aircraft hijacking">
        skyjacker
       </a>
       known to the public as
       <a href="/wiki/D._B._Cooper" title="D. B. Cooper">
        D. B. Cooper
       </a>
       , based on a misidentified report of his fictional boarding name of
       <a href="/wiki/Dan_Cooper_(comics)" title="Dan Cooper (comics)">
        Dan Cooper
       </a>
       ; collected a ransom of US$200,000 and then parachuted from the rear stairs of a
       <a href="/wiki/Boeing_727" title="Boeing 727">
        Boeing 727
       </a>
       at a height of 10,000 feet (3,000m) over the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Northwest" title="Pacific Northwest">
        Pacific Northwest
       </a>
       region of the United States, somewhere between
       <a href="/wiki/Seattle" title="Seattle">
        Seattle
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Portland,_Oregon" title="Portland, Oregon">
        Portland, Oregon
       </a>
       , 24 November.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77">
        <a href="#cite_note-77">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         77
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Durst#Other_cases" title="Robert Durst">
        Lynne Schulze
       </a>
       , 18, a student at
       <a href="/wiki/Middlebury_College" title="Middlebury College">
        Middlebury College
       </a>
       in Vermont, was last seen by one of her college friends on 10 December when she abruptly turned back on the way to a literature exam, claiming she had left her favorite pen in her dorm room, where her wallet, checkbook and other personal belongings were later found. A later report said that she was seen a short time later outside a health food store co-owned and operated at that time by
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Durst" title="Robert Durst">
        Robert Durst
       </a>
       and his wife Kathleen, herself disappeared a decade later. She had also been seen buying prunes from the same store earlier in the day. The case was reopened in 1992; in 2015, following Durst's arrest on charges of murdering his friend
       <a href="/wiki/Susan_Berman" title="Susan Berman">
        Susan Berman
       </a>
       , Middlebury police confirmed that they wanted to speak to Durst about the case, but his lawyer has declined to let them do so.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-NBCSchulze_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-NBCSchulze-78">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         78
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1972">
       1972
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: 1972">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Hale_Boggs" title="Hale Boggs">
        Hale Boggs
       </a>
       (58), US House Majority Leader (D-LA), and
       <a href="/wiki/Nick_Begich" title="Nick Begich">
        Nick Begich
       </a>
       (40), U.S. Representative from Alaska, disappeared with their
       <a href="/wiki/Cessna_310" title="Cessna 310">
        Cessna 310
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/Alaska" title="Alaska">
        Alaska
       </a>
       , along with Begich's aide Russell Brown and pilot Don Jonz, presumably on 16 October.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Zahir_Raihan" title="Zahir Raihan">
        Zahir Raihan
       </a>
       (36), Bangladeshi filmmaker, went looking for his brother
       <a href="/wiki/Shahidullah_Kaiser" title="Shahidullah Kaiser">
        Shahidullah Kaiser
       </a>
       and never returned.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1973">
       1973
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: 1973">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Anna_Christian_Waters" title="Anna Christian Waters">
        Anna Christian Waters
       </a>
       (5), disappeared from her backyard in Purisima Canyon, a rural area near
       <a href="/wiki/Half_Moon_Bay,_California" title="Half Moon Bay, California">
        Half Moon Bay
       </a>
       , California.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Beaumont_children_disappearance#Possibly_related_cases" title="Beaumont children disappearance">
        Joanne Ratcliffe
       </a>
       (11) and
       <a href="/wiki/Beaumont_children_disappearance#Possibly_related_cases" title="Beaumont children disappearance">
        Kirsty Gordon
       </a>
       (4) attended a football match at
       <a href="/wiki/Adelaide_Oval" title="Adelaide Oval">
        Adelaide Oval
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/South_Australia" title="South Australia">
        South Australia
       </a>
       , and then disappeared.
      </li>
      <li>
       Civil rights activist
       <a href="/wiki/Perry_Ray_Robinson" title="Perry Ray Robinson">
        Perry Ray Robinson
       </a>
       (35) disappeared during the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wounded_Knee_Incident" title="Wounded Knee Incident">
        Wounded Knee Incident
       </a>
       in South Dakota. It is believed that he was killed, perhaps executed for violating some of the terms of the occupiers, and he has been declared legally dead although his body has never been located. His family has sued the government to force the release of information, some of which seems to confirm that he was killed during the standoff.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Perry_Robinson_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Perry_Robinson-79">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         79
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1974">
       1974
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: 1974">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Zeta_Acosta" title="Oscar Zeta Acosta">
        Oscar Zeta Acosta
       </a>
       (39), American
       <a href="/wiki/Lawyer" title="Lawyer">
        attorney
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Chicano" title="Chicano">
        Chicano
       </a>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Activist" title="Activist">
        activist
       </a>
       , famously portrayed as "Dr. Gonzo" in
       <a href="/wiki/Hunter_S._Thompson" title="Hunter S. Thompson">
        Hunter S. Thompson
       </a>
       's book,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Fear_and_Loathing_in_Las_Vegas" title="Fear and Loathing in Las Vegas">
         Fear and Loathing in Las Vegas
        </a>
       </i>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Richard_John_Bingham,_7th_Earl_of_Lucan" title="Richard John Bingham, 7th Earl of Lucan">
        The 7th Earl of Lucan
       </a>
       (39), the last person indicted for murder by a
       <a href="/wiki/Inquest" title="Inquest">
        coroner's jury
       </a>
       . His whereabouts have been unknown since 7 November 1974, the night his children's nanny, Sandra Rivett, was beaten to death with a lead pipe in the basement of his estranged wife's home. Lord Lucan was
       <a href="/wiki/Declared_death_in_absentia" title="Declared death in absentia">
        officially declared dead
       </a>
       in 1999.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80">
        <a href="#cite_note-80">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         80
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Connie_Converse" title="Connie Converse">
        Connie Converse
       </a>
       (50), American singer-songwriter active in
       <a href="/wiki/New_York" title="New York">
        New York
       </a>
       in the 1950s. After writing a series of letters to family and friends alluding to dissatisfaction with her current life, she packed her belongings into her
       <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Beetle" title="Volkswagen Beetle">
        Volkswagen Beetle
       </a>
       and drove off, never to be heard from again.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1975">
       1975
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>

       </span>

     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Bas_Jan_Ader" title="Bas Jan Ader">

       </a>

       <a href="/wiki/Pocket_cruiser" title="Pocket cruiser">
        pocket cruiser
       </a>
       across the Atlantic.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Mona_Blades_case" title="Mona Blades case">
        Mona Blades
       </a>
       (18), New Zealander, disappeared while hitchhiking in the
       <a href="/wiki/North_Island" title="North Island">
        North Island
       </a>
       . Believed murdered, but no remains have ever been discovered.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Jimmy_Hoffa#Disappearance" title="Jimmy Hoffa">
        Jimmy Hoffa
       </a>
       (62), U.S. trade union leader, president of the
       <a href="/wiki/International_Brotherhood_of_Teamsters" title="International Brotherhood of Teamsters">
        International Brotherhood of Teamsters
       </a>
       , disappeared from the parking lot of a restaurant, where it is believed he was to meet with two Mafia leaders
       <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Giacalone" title="Anthony Giacalone">
        Anthony Giacalone
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Anthony_Provenzano" title="Anthony Provenzano">
        Anthony Provenzano
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81">
        <a href="#cite_note-81">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         81
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Lyon_sisters" title="Lyon sisters">
        The Lyon sisters
       </a>
       , Katherine Mary (10) and Sheila Mary (12), disappeared while walking home after visiting a nearby mall in the suburbs of
       <a href="/wiki/Washington,_D.C." title="Washington, D.C.">
        Washington, D.C.
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Juanita_Nielsen" title="Juanita Nielsen">
        Juanita Nielsen
       </a>
       (38), Australian publisher and anti-development campaigner, disappeared from
       <a href="/wiki/Kings_Cross,_New_South_Wales" title="Kings Cross, New South Wales">
        Kings Cross
       </a>
       , Sydney.
      </li>
     </ul>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1978">
       1978
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: 1978">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Trudie_Adams" title="Disappearance of Trudie Adams">
        Trudie Adams
       </a>
       (18) was last seen getting into a van while hitching a ride home from a dance in
       <a href="/wiki/Newport,_New_South_Wales" title="Newport, New South Wales">
        Newport, New South Wales
       </a>
       , Australia on 24 June. She is believed to have been abducted.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Eddie_Aikau" title="Eddie Aikau">
        Eddie Aikau
       </a>
       (31), a Hawaiian life guard and surfer. After the crash of the
       <i>
        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hokule%27a" title="Hokule'a">
         Hokule'a
        </a>
       </i>
       , Aikau paddled out to get help from the nearest island,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lanai,_Hawaii" title="Lanai, Hawaii">
        Lanai
       </a>
       , and was never seen again. The people aboard the
       <i>
        Hokule'a
       </i>
       were saved by air.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/John_Brisker" title="John Brisker">
        John Brisker
       </a>
       (31), former
       <a href="/wiki/American_Basketball_Association" title="American Basketball Association">

       </a>

       <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">
        National Basketball Association
       </a>
       player, disappeared after flying to
       <a href="/wiki/Uganda" title="Uganda">
        Uganda
       </a>
       . He was declared legally dead in 1985.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Valentich_disappearance" title="Valentich disappearance">
        Frederick Valentich
       </a>
       (21) disappeared during a solo flight over the
       <a href="/wiki/Bass_Strait" title="Bass Strait">
        Bass Strait
       </a>
       in Australia, after reporting to an air traffic controller that his plane was being circled by an unknown craft.

       </a>

     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1979">
       1979
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: 1979">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Etan_Patz" title="Disappearance of Etan Patz">
        Etan Patz
       </a>
       (6), disappeared while on his way to school in lower
       <a href="/wiki/Manhattan" title="Manhattan">
        Manhattan
       </a>
       . By 2001, he was considered legally dead. He was the first missing child featured on a milk carton.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90">
        <a href="#cite_note-90">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         90
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       In May 2012, authorities re-opened the case.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91">
        <a href="#cite_note-91">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         91
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Pedro Hernandez, 51, was charged with second-degree murder in Patz's death, based largely on a signed confession he gave after he spoke voluntarily to detectives for hours, according to police. However, Patz's body, which Hernandez said he put in the trash, has not been recovered.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Ian_Mackintosh" title="Ian Mackintosh">
        Ian Mackintosh
       </a>
       , creator and writer of
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/The_Sandbaggers" title="The Sandbaggers">
         The Sandbaggers
        </a>
       </i>
       British television series, was flying with two others over the Gulf of Alaska in a light aircraft in July 1979. The plane sent out a distress signal, which was picked up by the United States Coast Guard. The plane's last-known position was searched, but no wreckage of the plane was ever found, and its passengers have not been heard from since.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92">
        <a href="#cite_note-92">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         92
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Martin_Allen" title="Disappearance of Martin Allen">
        Martin Allen
       </a>
       , 15-year-old British boy, disappeared while travelling home on the
       <a href="/wiki/London_Underground" title="London Underground">
        London Underground
       </a>
       . Despite a large-scale police operation at the time of his disappearance and a renewed appeal in 2009, no trace of Allen was ever found and his fate remains unknown.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h2>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1980s">
       1980s
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: 1980s">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h2>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1980">
       1980
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: 1980">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Alan_Addis" title="Alan Addis">
        Alan Addis
       </a>
       (19) was a British soldier serving with the
       <a href="/wiki/Royal_Marines" title="Royal Marines">
        Royal Marines
       </a>
       in the
       <a href="/wiki/Falkland_Islands" title="Falkland Islands">
        Falkland Islands
       </a>
       . He disappeared without trace in August 1980 in a remote settlement on
       <a href="/wiki/East_Falkland" title="East Falkland">
        East Falkland
       </a>
       . Several local men were arrested and released without being charged several years later; the investigation continues.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azaria_Chamberlain" title="Azaria Chamberlain">
        Azaria Chamberlain
       </a>
       , nine-week-old Australian baby girl. Her remains have never been found. Azaria's mother Lindy Chamberlain insisted that a
       <a href="/wiki/Dingo" title="Dingo">
        dingo
       </a>
       took her baby from her camping tent near
       <a href="/wiki/Uluru" title="Uluru">
        Uluru
       </a>
       . In a trial sensationalised by the media, Lindy was found guilty of murder and sentenced to life. Her sentence was overturned six years later when Azaria's jacket was found in a dingo lair. Azaria's disappearance was the subject of four inquests, the last of which, in 2012, concurred that a dingo had taken and killed her.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93">
        <a href="#cite_note-93">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         93
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Azaria's disappearance and the subsequent police investigation were the basis for the 1988 motion picture
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Evil_Angels_(film)" title="Evil Angels (film)">
         Evil Angels
        </a>
       </i>
       (released as
       <i>
        A Cry in the Dark
       </i>
       outside of Australia and New Zealand
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94">
        <a href="#cite_note-94">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         94
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       ).
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Louise_and_Charmian_Faulkner_disappearance" title="Louise and Charmian Faulkner disappearance">
        Louise and Charmian Faulkner
       </a>
       , mother (43) and daughter (2), disappeared from outside their home in
       <a href="/wiki/St_Kilda,_Victoria" title="St Kilda, Victoria">
        St Kilda
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Melbourne" title="Melbourne">
        Melbourne
       </a>
       , Australia.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1981">
       1981
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=30" title="Edit section: 1981">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Katrice_Lee" title="Disappearance of Katrice Lee">
        Katrice Lee
       </a>
       disappeared from a
       <a href="/wiki/Navy,_Army_and_Air_Force_Institutes" title="Navy, Army and Air Force Institutes">
        NAAFI
       </a>
       shopping complex in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Schlo%C3%9F_Neuhaus" title="Schlo Neuhaus">
        Schlo Neuhaus
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Paderborn" title="Paderborn">
        Paderborn
       </a>
       in
       <a href="/wiki/West_Germany" title="West Germany">
        West Germany
       </a>
       on 28 November 1981, the day of her second birthday.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1982">
       1982
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=31" title="Edit section: 1982">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       On 31 January 1982, Kathleen McCormack Durst, 29, a medical student, left the Connecticut house of a friend to return to the
       <a href="/wiki/South_Salem,_New_York" title="South Salem, New York">
        South Salem, New York
       </a>
       , residence she shared with her husband,
       <a href="/wiki/Robert_Durst" title="Robert Durst">
        Robert Durst
       </a>
       , the wealthy heir to a New York City real estate fortune. The marriage had been deteriorating for some time due to his increasingly violent behavior and her friends had been urging her to leave it; when she left she warned them to call the police if anything happened. Durst says when she returned, he drove her to a nearby train station so she could return to the couple's Manhattan apartment and she called him from there after she arrived; a doorman says he saw her at the building the following day but could not confirm the sighting. Four days later, Durst reported her absence to police. She has not been seen since and was declared legally dead in 2001. Police strongly suspect Durst of murdering her (and, 18 years later,
       <a href="/wiki/Susan_Berman" title="Susan Berman">
        Susan Berman
       </a>
       ) due to inconsistencies in his story.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Charley_Project_Durst_page_95-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Charley_Project_Durst_page-95">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         95
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Gosch" title="Johnny Gosch">
        Johnny Gosch
       </a>
       (12) was reported missing to
       <a href="/wiki/West_Des_Moines,_Iowa" title="West Des Moines, Iowa">
        West Des Moines
       </a>
       Police Department
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96">
        <a href="#cite_note-96">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         96
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       by his parents after he disappeared while delivering newspapers. At that time, there was a customary three-day waiting period before police responded to missing persons reports. Gosch was never heard from again, but his case prompted new laws for Iowa and other states, resulting in missing persons reports involving children being given immediate attention.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97">
        <a href="#cite_note-97">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         97
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Tony_Jones" title="Disappearance of Tony Jones">
        Tony Jones
       </a>
       (20) disappeared on 3 November from
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Townsville,_Queensland" title="Townsville, Queensland">
        Townsville, Queensland
       </a>
       , while backpacking around Australia.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Ahmad_Motevaselian" title="Ahmad Motevaselian">
        Ahmad Motevaselian
       </a>
       was an Iranian military attache and one of the three Iranian diplomats (
       <a href="/wiki/Seyed_Mohsen_Mousavi" title="Seyed Mohsen Mousavi">
        Seyed Mohsen Mousavi
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Kazem_Akhavan" title="Kazem Akhavan">
        Kazem Akhavan
       </a>
       , and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Taghi_Rastegar_Moghadam" title="Taghi Rastegar Moghadam">
        Taghi Rastegar Moghadam
       </a>
       ) that disappeared in
       <a href="/wiki/Lebanon" title="Lebanon">
        Lebanon
       </a>
       in 1982. On 5 July 1982, when the vehicle carrying the diplomats was passing through a checkpoint post on its way to
       <a href="/wiki/Beirut" title="Beirut">
        Beirut
       </a>
       , it was intercepted by
       <a href="/wiki/Kataeb_Party" title="Kataeb Party">
        Phalange Party
       </a>
       members. Three decades after the incident, the fate of the missing diplomats remains a mystery, and the search for Motevaselian and the other Iranian diplomats continues.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hezbollah_98-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hezbollah-98">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         98
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Roknabadi_99-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Roknabadi-99">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         99
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamshahri_100-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamshahri-100">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         100
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1983">
       1983
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=32" title="Edit section: 1983">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Upali_Wijewardene" title="Upali Wijewardene">
        Upali Wijewardene
       </a>
       , a well-known Sri Lankan businessman, disappeared on 13 February 1983 on a flight from Subang international Airport (Malaysia) to
       <a href="/wiki/Sri_Lanka" title="Sri Lanka">
        Sri Lanka
       </a>
       in his private jet.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Emanuela_Orlandi" title="Disappearance of Emanuela Orlandi">
        Emanuela Orlandi
       </a>
       (15), citizen of
       <a href="/wiki/Vatican_City" title="Vatican City">
        Vatican City
       </a>
       . Her mysterious disappearance has been linked both to sexual exploitation as well as an attempt to demand the release of
       <a href="/wiki/Mehmet_Ali_A%C4%9Fca" title="Mehmet Ali Aca">
        Mehmet Ali Aca
       </a>
       from prison.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Mirella_Gregori" title="Disappearance of Mirella Gregori">
        Mirella Gregori
       </a>
       (15) mysteriously disappeared from Rome during the spring of 1983, about 40 days before
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Emanuela_Orlandi" title="Emanuela Orlandi">
        Emanuela Orlandi
       </a>
       vanished. The two cases are believed to be linked.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Kirsa_Jensen_case" title="Kirsa Jensen case">
        Kirsa Jensen
       </a>
       (14) disappeared while riding her horse to a beach near
       <a href="/wiki/Napier,_New_Zealand" title="Napier, New Zealand">
        Napier, New Zealand
       </a>
       .
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Tammy_Lynn_Leppert" title="Tammy Lynn Leppert">
        Tammy Lynn Leppert
       </a>
       (18) a model and actress who disappeared without a trace after leaving her
       <a href="/wiki/Rockledge,_Florida" title="Rockledge, Florida">
        Rockledge, Florida
       </a>
       , family home.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101">
        <a href="#cite_note-101">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         101
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Ann_Gotlib" title="Ann Gotlib">
        Ann Gotlib
       </a>
       (12), was a Russian immigrant who disappeared from the premises of a Louisville, Kentucky mall on 1 June 1983.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1984">
       1984
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=33" title="Edit section: 1984">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Kevin_Andrew_Collins" title="Kevin Andrew Collins">
        Kevin Andrew Collins
       </a>
       (10) disappeared while returning home alone from basketball practice at his school in the Haight district of San Francisco. His was one of the first of the "Have you seen me?" milk carton photos.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Edward_L._Montoro" title="Edward L. Montoro">
        Edward L. Montoro
       </a>
       (52) motion picture producer/distributor, disappeared after taking more than $1 million from his own company,
       <a href="/wiki/Film_Ventures_International" title="Film Ventures International">
        Film Ventures International
       </a>
       . It was speculated that he fled to Mexico, but his whereabouts to this day have been undetermined.
      </li>
     </ul>
     <h3>
      <span class="mw-headline" id="1985">
       1985
      </span>
      <span class="mw-editsection">
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        [
       </span>
       <a href="/w/index.php?title=List_of_people_who_disappeared_mysteriously&amp;action=edit&amp;section=34" title="Edit section: 1985">
        edit
       </a>
       <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
        ]
       </span>
      </span>
     </h3>
     <ul>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Disappearance_of_Cherrie_Mahan" title="Disappearance of Cherrie Mahan">
        Cherrie Mahan
       </a>
       (8), disappeared on 22 February 1985 after getting off a school bus along a road in rural Winfield Township, Butler County,
       <a href="/wiki/Pennsylvania" title="Pennsylvania">
        Pennsylvania
       </a>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Boris_Weisfeiler" title="Boris Weisfeiler">
        Boris Weisfeiler
       </a>
       (43), U.S. mathematician, disappeared in the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biob%C3%ADo_Region" title="Biobo Region">
        Biobo Region
       </a>
       of
       <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">
        Chile
       </a>
       during a solo
       <a href="/wiki/Hiking" title="Hiking">
        hiking
       </a>
       trip.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102">
        <a href="#cite_note-102">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         102
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
       Chilean authorities originally concluded that he drowned, but documents released by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_States_Department_of_State" title="United States Department of State">
        United States Department of State
       </a>
       in 2000 included a 1986 memo suggesting he may be a captive "somewhere in Chile (probably
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Colonia_Dignidad" title="Colonia Dignidad">
        Colonia Dignidad
       </a>
       )", and a 1987 account by a
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/CIA" title="CIA">
        CIA
       </a>
       source claiming that Weisfeiler had been interrogated and fatally beaten by a Chilean army patrol.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103">
        <a href="#cite_note-103">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         103
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Vladimir_Alexandrov" title="Vladimir Alexandrov">
        Vladimir Alexandrov
       </a>
       , Russian
       <a href="/wiki/Physicist" title="Physicist">
        physicist
       </a>
       , disappeared while attending a
       <a href="/wiki/Nuclear_winter" title="Nuclear winter">
        nuclear winter
       </a>
       conference in
       <a href="/wiki/Madrid" title="Madrid">
        Madrid
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104">
        <a href="#cite_note-104">
         <span>
          [
         </span>
         104
         <span>
          ]
         </span>
        </a>
       </sup>
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Dale_Flannery" title="Christopher Dale Flannery">
        Christopher Dale Flannery
       </a>
       , a famous figure of the Australian underworld and an alleged hitman who was responsible for numerous murders, exited his apartment in May 1985 to meet with his employer and was never seen again.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Diane_Suzuki" title="Diane Suzuki">
        Diane Suzuki
       </a>
       (19), dancer and student at the University of Hawai'i at Mnoa disappeared on 6 July 1985 after leaving the dance school where she taught. Blood evidence was found at the scene, but no body has ever been found.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Andrew_Fluegelman" title="Andrew Fluegelman">
        Andrew Fluegelman
       </a>
       (41), was a publisher, photographer, programmer and attorney best known as a pioneer of what is now known as the "shareware" business model for software marketing. On the afternoon of 6 July 1985, he left his office in Tiburon, California. A week later, his abandoned car was found at the north end of the Golden Gate Bridge near San Francisco. His family held a memorial service for Fluegelman, and he is presumed dead, though his body has never been found.
      </li>
      <li>
       <a href="/wiki/Cotah_Ramaswami" title="Cotah Ramaswami">
        Cotah Ramaswami
       </a>
       (89), Indian cricketer who played in
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Indian_cricket_team" title="Indian cricket team">
        India
       </a>
       's first test match in 1932. He walked out of his home in
       <a href="/wiki/Chennai" title="Chennai">
        Chennai
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/India" title="India">
        India
       </a>
       , on 15 October 1985 and was never seen again.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105">
        <a href="#cite_note-105">
         <span>
